Current Affairs Commentary

Reading the Declaration of the Beiping Cultural and Educational Circles

— Bing

More than twenty figures from the Beiping cultural and educational circles, including Chiang Meng-lin, Fu Szu-nien, Hu Shih, and Chiang Ting-fu, recently issued a declaration stating, "We resolutely oppose all conspiracies and actions that detach from the central government and establish special political organizations. We demand that the government use the power of the whole country to maintain the territorial and administrative integrity of the country." The language is extremely concise, and a spirit of integrity naturally flows from the words. Today, when the so-called "Jidong Anti-Communist Autonomous Committee" has already appeared in North China, reading it feels particularly inspiring. The demands of our people, though numerous, when measured to the lowest and most minimal extent, and what must be fulfilled, are only the few words mentioned in this declaration.

Most intellectuals are fond of engaging in empty theories. When they comment on current affairs, "China" and "China" are constantly on their lips and in their writings, accompanied by reckless accusations and endless criticisms of shortcomings. Listening to their words and reading their articles leaves people scratching their heads, at a loss as to what to do. Yet, they remain aloof, as if they do not belong to any nationality. To conceal illness and avoid treatment is certainly wrong. However, when making pronouncements, one should pay attention to the actual situation at this time and in this place. The current state of our country is far from satisfactory; who does not know this? However, the blame for this should not be placed on any single individual or group. All those who are called Chinese bear some responsibility on their shoulders. Therefore, the most important thing today is that even if we cannot but condemn all realities, we must, in addition to condemnation, devise ways to handle the situation ourselves. The meaning is very clear: China belongs to the Chinese people.

Most intellectuals are also fond of seeking compromise and temporary peace. In the past, someone proposed making Beiping a cultural city, which is the strongest evidence of this idea. Moreover, people in the South believe that a crisis is lurking in North China, and they do not want to send their children to study in northern schools, which is a concrete manifestation of this mentality. How could they know that all these acts of passively accepting misfortune only serve to encourage those with ambitions to intensify their aggression? If the whole country were like this, iron hooves would gallop as if entering a land without people. Hu Shih once said, "Although the ceasefire in North China cannot make the enemy withdraw an inch from the four eastern provinces, at least it should prevent them from occupying an inch of land outside the four eastern provinces." Recently, Hu Shih said with emotion, "Now it seems, I was completely wrong." (See the *Ta Kung Pao* weekly essay on the 17th of this month.) Although Hu Shih blames the neglect of defense work, he may deeply regret his previous stance of concession and lack of psychological defense. Therefore, in the declaration he signed, there is the phrase "use the power of the whole country to maintain the territorial and administrative integrity of the country." This transformation is truly related to the future life of our nation. Having confidence in our strength and using it well is the key to survival.

Japanese Troops in Yuguan Post Public Notices to Reassure the People

(Beiping) A report from Yuguan states that the Japanese troops arriving in Yuguan from Jin County and Suizhong appear to be stationed there for a long time. On the 27th, they posted notices in Linyu City to reassure the people. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Matsui Brigade of the Japanese army, newly arrived in Shanhaiguan, issued a notice stating that the army conducts public buying and selling, and anyone with information about illegal activities is allowed to report them. (28th Special Dispatch)

Expansion of the South Manchuria Railway Tianjin Office Completed

(Tianjin) The South Manchuria Railway Tianjin Office moved into the fifth floor of the Xinhua Building in the French Concession on the 28th. The expansion has been completed, and it is now open for business. (28th Special Dispatch)

Tianjin Public Security Bureau Strictly Crack Down on Hoarding of Copper Coins

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Municipal Public Security Bureau issued an order on the 28th to all districts to strictly crack down on the hoarding of copper coins and the use of paper notes instead. The Hebei Provincial Bank is still considering issuing copper coin notes. (28th Special Dispatch)

Fu Zuoyi Calls on Yan to Report on Recent Situation in Sui Politics

(Taiyuan) Fu Zuoyi returned to Bing from Sui this afternoon and called on the cabinet that evening to report on the recent situation in Sui politics and to ask for instructions on the current situation. According to reports, he will stay in Bing for about three to five days. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Taiyuan) The two provincial offices of Sui previously ordered all counties to send representatives to form an inspection group on the bandit situation in northern Shaanxi. They traveled to Shaanxi and back for more than twenty days and returned to Bing last night. According to reports, the bandit situation in northern Shaanxi is very fierce, with bandits and civilians indistinguishable, and residents displaced, in a very difficult situation. They are currently preparing a report and will return to their counties to publicize it after visiting Yan for instructions, in order to awaken the people. It is confirmed that bandits are lurking in the counties along the river in western Shanxi, and winter defense is worrying. Sun Chu is scheduled to return to Bing within a few days to visit Yan and report. Qu Youcheng, the regimental commander of Sun's troops, was killed in a fierce battle with bandits in Wubao on the 17th of this month. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Taiyuan) According to military news from the front, Liu Zidan, the bandit leader in northern Shaanxi, was recently killed by Wang Yizhe's troops. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Taiyuan) Yan Xishan convened senior officials from the Sui government and provincial committee members this morning at the Sui government to inquire in detail about the recent military and political situation. He decided to return to the riverbank in three or two days to commemorate the anniversary of his late father's death. Chief Counselor Zhao Daiwen has recently been suffering from hemoptysis due to old age and overwork. Yan expressed his deep condolences and arranged for medical treatment. (28th Special Dispatch)

Wang Shu-chang, Jiao Yi-tang, etc. to Hold Supplementary Oath-Taking Ceremony Today; Chairman Lin Will Attend to Give Instructions

(Nanjing) Wang Shu-chang, Vice President of the Senate, Jiao Yi-tang, President of the Supreme Court, Shi Ying, Minister of the Ministry of Personnel, Li Zonghuang and Wang Qi, members of the Supervisory Committee, Niu Yongjian, Director of the First Examination Committee of this year's Higher Examination, Zhang Zhiben, member of the Examination Committee, Liu San, member of the Supervisory Committee, and Chen Daqi, Director of the First Examination Affairs Office, are scheduled to hold a supplementary oath-taking ceremony at the National Government at 10:00 am on the 29th. In addition to officials sent by the Central Government to supervise the oath-taking ceremony at the time, Chairman Lin will attend to give instructions. (28th Central News Agency Telegram)

He Jian Returns to Nanjing to Visit Chiang and Ask for Instructions on the Bandit Suppression Policy in Western Hunan

(Nanjing) He Jian went to Shanghai a few days ago. Now that the First Plenary Session of the Central Committee is about to open, he returned to Nanjing on the morning of the 28th and visited Chairman Chiang in the afternoon to ask for instructions on the policy of eliminating the remaining bandits in western Hunan. (28th Special Dispatch)

Nanjing and Hangzhou Jointly Conduct Air Defense Drills; Nighttime Light Control Implemented in Various Places; Anti-Air Raid Department Dispatches Aircraft to Reconnoiter Along Different Routes

(Nanjing) The joint air defense exercise between Nanjing and Hangzhou began on the morning of the 28th. During the day, Nanjing and Zhenjiang were training observation posts, air defense duties, and capabilities. Hangzhou simulated enemy aircraft attacking from a certain direction, practicing air combat and ground-to-air combat. During the nighttime exercise, strict light control was implemented in various places. The traffic control, evacuation control, fire protection, public works, and rescue teams in Nanjing were all concentrated and awaiting orders on the morning of the 28th. Evacuation shelters and rescue stations were also set up. The Boy Scouts of Nanjing departed in uniform to participate in the work. Around 9:00 am, the Air Defense Command dispatched aircraft to reconnoiter along four routes. Due to bad weather, navigation was difficult, and two routes flew back to Nanjing, while the other two completed their missions. In the afternoon, another aircraft was dispatched to Yiyi and completed its mission. Observation posts in various places reported their actions to the command at any time when aircraft flew over, which was extremely fast. (28th Central News Agency Telegram)

(Nanjing) Nanjing and Hangzhou began a joint air defense exercise on the 28th. A special commissioner of the Air Defense Command gave a broadcast speech, explaining the significance of the exercise and stating that the air defense exercise is to review the degree of air defense construction, the strength of air defense preparations, and to familiarize the general military and civilians with various air defense actions, in order to consolidate the city's air defense. In order for air defense measures to reach a satisfactory state, on the one hand, the government relies on the active use of flight teams and anti-aircraft artillery teams to attack enemy aircraft, and on the other hand, it relies on the assistance of the public in eliminating colors and preventing air raids: (1) Obey the guidance of the political and planning organs; (2) Strictly follow the matters that should be done in air defense; (3) Correctly implement the actions based on the air raid shelters. (28th Central News Agency Telegram)

(Nanjing) Yang Jie, the commander of the Air Defense Exercise, gave a radio address on the 28th, discussing the public's understanding of the air defense exercise, saying that the purpose of the exercise is: (1) To test whether the air force can resist or destroy enemy aircraft outside the airspace; (2) To practice and review whether the ground air defense forces can cope with enemy air raids; (3) To train the public to understand the cruelty of air warfare and methods of self-defense. (28th Central News Agency Telegram)

(Hangzhou) The air defense authorities received a military report from the observation post that enemy aircraft were attacking Hangzhou. Starting at 8:30, all military police and Boy Scouts were dispatched, and traffic on all roads in the city was cut off. The performance was completed at 10:30 and then restored. At 2:15 pm, the air defense authorities discovered two enemy aircraft attacking Hangzhou along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road. Our forces fired smoke bombs at the aircraft, and the enemy aircraft dropped bombs. In the evening, a light control performance was held, and the results were very good. (28th Special Dispatch)

Transfer of Affairs at the Dongzhuang Dike Closure Office is Underway

(Jinan) The provincial government has telegraphed the Economic Committee, ordering the dike closure association to transfer the dike closure affairs to the Yellow River Water Conservancy Association. (28th)

(Jinan) Zhang Honglie is scheduled to discuss the transfer with Kong Xiangrong on the 29th. Zhang said that the transfer of accounts is not difficult, but the inventory of materials is cumbersome. The retention or departure of staff is up to Kong. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) The Provincial Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Management Committee is scheduled to be established on the first of next month, with Li Shuchun designated as the chairman. (28th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Our embassy in Paris is located in a prosperous area, next to a theater, with noisy traffic all day long. When Minister Gu returned home, he requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to allocate funds to find another site. It was approved to build a new one. The site has been surveyed and the construction cost and land price are 120,000 yuan. (Fuzhou) The military campaign to suppress the Red bandits in eastern Fujian has entered its final stage. Each bandit force is being surrounded and suppressed by our various units and annihilation is imminent. In addition, the weather is gradually turning cold, and there is a shortage of food and clothing, making it difficult for them to survive. The various counties in Funing are very peaceful. The Huang Ligui faction of the pseudo-Independent Division has fled to northern Fujian. After being blocked and suppressed by the Liu and Zhou divisions, they gathered their remaining forces and planned to flee north through Pinggu into Zhejiang Province. In addition to ordering the Liu and Zhou divisions to track and pursue them, the military authorities have also ordered the troops in Zhejiang Province to send additional forces to intercept them. Aircraft "China" Stays in Guam for One Day; Continues to Manila the Next Morning

Guam: The large aircraft "China" arrived here today and will stay for one day to celebrate Thanksgiving. It will fly to Manila tomorrow. The distance from here to the Philippines is 1,500 kilometers and requires approximately 10 to 12 hours of flight, so the aircraft must take off at 6:30 tomorrow morning. (26th Kuomintang Telegram)

After the Breakup of the Manchuria Conference, the Mongolian Delegate Returned to Kulun; Refusing to Accept Unreasonable Demands from the Puppet Government Was the Reason for the Breakdown of the Negotiations

(Moscow) A report from Kulun states that the Manchuria-Mongolia Conference in Manchuria broke down again on November 25. The conference discussed the establishment of a Manchuria-Mongolia border committee and the exchange of representatives between the two sides. On the 25th, the "Manchurian" side refused to continue negotiations because the Mongolian side could not accept its final ultimatum-style request to send three representatives (one of whom was stationed in Kulun with the qualification of diplomatic representative). On the 26th, the Mongolian delegation, led by Sambu, rushed back to Kulun. According to well-informed sources in Mongolia, the reason for the breakdown of the negotiations was that the "Manchurian" side wanted to expand the scope of the negotiations beyond the original task. The Manchurian delegation did not discuss border issues, but rather demanded the establishment of Manchuria-Mongolia diplomatic relations in the form of an ultimatum. Although the "Manchurian" delegation later formally withdrew this request and agreed to limit the scope of negotiations to mediating border disputes, it still insisted on sending a "border" delegate to Kulun (Kulun is 1,000 kilometers from the border) in the form of an ultimatum. This actually maintains the original proposal, demanding recognition of the puppet state and the establishment of diplomatic relations. According to reports, the "Manchurian state" has not established diplomatic relations with other countries (including its neighbors), so the attitude of the "Manchurian government" is extremely surprising. At the same time, "Manchuria" has not issued any similar ultimatum to any country, nor has it made demands to intimidate with military action. Even if they were to exchange actual envoys, it would not contribute to peace and friendship. For example, China and Japan still maintain diplomatic relations to this day, but they have no normal and friendly relations. (28th TASS Telegram)

A Safe in the Soviet Embassy in Czechoslovakia Was Stolen

Prague: The Soviet Ambassador here, Alexander Alexandrovsky, discovered today that the safe in his embassy had been searched and important secret documents had been lost.

Art Ramblings

Imagery Beauty (Continued)

— Feng Zikai

My memory isn't so bad when it comes to the poetry and prose of the ancients. I can still recall quite a few examples. I've also excerpted some below for contemplation:

On the day the Taiping Scholar returns,

He and the Emperor shall untie robes of war.

One hundred forty thousand men all laid down their armor,

Not a single one was a man.

I strongly wish to follow you, but I'm too old,

I'll use illness as an excuse to resign from office.

Beneath Yanling Terrace, the Tongjiang River flows,

How many people untie their fishing lines to catch bass?

Year after year, war bones are buried in the wilderness,

Only to see grapes enter the Han court.

If Heaven's will is so, then let us enjoy the cup.

How can I obtain a ten-thousand-mile fur coat

To cover the four borders of the land?

Could the ruler bear to give up the conquest of Chen,

And only occupy a few acres of fields in Leithang?

Swallows before the halls of the old Wang and Xie families,

Fly into the homes of ordinary people.

Life in this world is not always satisfactory,

Tomorrow I will let my hair down and sail a small boat.

Who wept the most in the gathering?

The Jiangzhou Sima's green robe was wet with tears.

When shall we trim the western window candles together,

And talk about the night rain of Bashan?

Night rain trims spring chives,

New rice is cooked with yellow millet.

A guest comes from afar,

His clothes are covered in the rain of Baling.

The city cannot bear the arrival of the traveling monk,

Lest he startle the orioles before the painted tower.

I have three hundred Wu writing papers in my box,

I plan to use delicate strokes to express my spring sorrow.

If she could understand the love of extravagance,

She would freeze to death in the house of gold. (Ode to a Silkworm Woman)

From afar, I see the curtains of the main hall opening,

Palace women in robes and trousers sweep the imperial bed.

I bitterly hate pressing gold thread year after year,

Making wedding clothes for others.

Pingyang's singing and dancing newly receive favor,

Beyond the curtain, the spring cold bestows brocade robes.

If the east wind did not favor Zhou Lang,

The bronze sparrow terrace would lock up the two Qiaos in the depths of spring.

You come from my hometown,

You should know the affairs of my hometown.

The day you left, before the patterned window,

Did the winter plum blossoms bloom? I have a silk dress, Made when the Qin king was alive, I danced in the spring breeze a lot, But now in the autumn is no longer suitable. Hit the yellow oriole, Do not let it chirp on the branches. When it chirps, it disturbs my dreams, And I cannot reach Liaoxi.

The so-called "The Emperor and the General untie war robes" – is it really just untying war robes? It uses this concrete, trivial, and simple matter to suggest great rewards like promotions and riches. And does the Emperor really need to personally untie the war robes? Saying that he is willing to untie war robes implies great rewards, without the need to actually untie them. But to speak abstractly about great rewards is uninteresting; to speak concretely about untying war robes has poetic appeal. Similarly, "all lay down their armor" is the concrete way of saying they all surrendered, "resigning from office" is the concrete way of saying they resigned their positions, and "untying fishing lines to catch bass" is the concrete way of saying they were willing to live in seclusion. Poets best understand the secret of seeing the big picture in small things and the whole in individual cases; they are best at using a small, concrete matter to suggest a larger, abstract one. Saying "How can I obtain a ten-thousand-mile fur coat" reveals the desire to save the world. Saying "Swallows before the halls fly into the homes of ordinary people" reveals the decline of the halls and their people. Saying "green robe is wet" reveals the sorrow. Saying "sweep the imperial bed" and "bestows brocade robes" reveals the favor. Saying "locks up the two Qiaos" reveals the victory. At the same time, because these small events are all concrete, trivial, and simple, they can give the reader a definite, strong, vivid, and lively impression. After reading "trim the western window candles together" and "night rain trims spring chives," one can imagine the various sentiments of old friends reuniting after a long separation, drinking wine and talking under the lamp, as if one were there in person. Especially the last three five-character quatrains are entirely imagery beauty. The first only mentions "winter plum blossoms," the second only mentions a single "silk dress," and the third only mentions "hitting the yellow oriole." And the feelings of missing home, lamenting the passage of time, and longing for someone far away stand out clearly behind these small matters, deeply impressing themselves on the reader's mind.

From the perspective of the arts, music focuses on auditory beauty, i.e., the beauty of sound; painting focuses on visual beauty, i.e., the beauty of form; and literature focuses on the beauty of thought, i.e., the beauty of language. Then the so-called "imagery beauty" logically belongs in the realm of painting. Painting, apart from Cubism and Constructivism, often contains a large amount of the beauty of thought, i.e., the beauty of meaning, while literature, as mentioned above, also makes great use of imagery beauty. This can be seen as an exchange between literature and painting, a handshake between literature and painting. I once wrote a book "Literature and Painting" (Kaiming edition) discussing the various interactions between literature and painting. That was already two or three years ago. Now I have discovered another kind of interaction as described above, and I feel the interest of those days growing thick again.

Page 6

League of Nations Vigorously Seeks to Shorten the War by Expanding Sanctions; Oil Added to the List of Prohibited Items; US Support Facilitates Success; Eighteen-Nation Committee to Meet Next Month to Decide on Implementation Date

(Geneva) It is expected that the Eighteen-Nation Committee will convene on September 12 to consider the issue of an oil embargo. Hungary and Lithuania have also notified the League of Nations that they have resolved to implement full sanctions against Italy. (Reuters, 28th)

(Geneva) League of Nations officials believe that the Eighteen-Nation Committee will decide to implement the oil embargo soon. Although Italian headquarters troops have been moving recently, their purpose is to threaten any resolutions the League of Nations may adopt, and they are unlikely to have any impact. (Havas, 28th)

(London) Official sources here state that after the US government decided to limit the amount of oil it exports to warring countries, the League of Nations will find it easier to initiate an oil embargo against Italy, and the decision is expected sooner than anticipated. The British government previously hesitated to urge the League of Nations to proceed with this matter quickly, fearing that the US Congress might object later. Now that the US executive branch has taken action, the situation is different. The US will definitely support the League of Nations' efforts to maintain peace. The US Congress, when it reconvenes next January, will also support President Roosevelt's proposal to include oil in the list of prohibited goods. Furthermore, when the British Ambassador to France, Clark, met with French Premier Laval yesterday, the content of their discussion likely concerned both the oil embargo and the mutual assistance between Britain and France in the Mediterranean. (Havas, 28th)

(London) Authorities here received news today that Italian troops will soon occupy the Lake Tana region. Lake Tana is the source of the Blue Nile, on which Egypt and Sudan rely for irrigation. Therefore, after the occupation, Britain will regard Italy as violating its promises, as well as violating the 1906 treaty dividing the economic spheres of influence in Abyssinia and the documents exchanged between Britain and Italy in 1925. It is also understood that a full cabinet meeting has decided to find ways to enable member states of the League of Nations to implement an oil embargo against Italy as soon as possible. Foreign Secretary Hoare has also asked US representative Atherton to assure that the sanctions committee will likely convene in early December to discuss the immediate oil embargo against Italy. (National News, 27th)

(Washington) The US government has refused permission for the oil tanker Ulysses to sail to Italy carrying oil, and a dispute has apparently arisen between the US and Italy. However, diplomatic circles remain tight-lipped today. Well-informed observers believe today that Italian Ambassador Rosso has protested to Secretary of State Hull about this matter. However, both the State Department and the Italian Embassy are unwilling to confirm this news. One official said that this matter is too complicated to discuss. Diplomats here believe that this already implicitly acknowledges that a dispute has arisen between the two parties. The US Director of Transportation, Peacock, stated that "the status of the Ulysses remains unchanged," which shows that the US attitude is quite firm. (National News, 27th)

Hungarian Premier Visits Vienna to Discuss Economic Issues Between the Two Countries

Budapest: Prime Minister Gömbös and Foreign Minister Kánya are scheduled to visit Vienna tomorrow to confer with Austrian Chancellor Schuschnigg. (Havas, 27th)

(Vienna) Hungarian Prime Minister Gömbös and Foreign Minister Kánya will arrive here tomorrow to visit Prime Minister Schuschnigg. Although official sources here state that the visit of Hungarian dignitaries is of a social nature, as cabinet members of Austria and Hungary routinely exchange visits and exchange views after a certain period, semi-official sources believe that the prime ministers of Austria and Hungary will discuss the economic situation of the two countries and plan to discuss the common attitude that the two countries will adopt towards the sanctions issue. (Havas, 27th)

Japanese Company Leases Cotton Fields in Dutch New Guinea; Dutch Officials Say There Is No Need to Overreact

The Hague: Government officials stated today that while there is concern that Japan will gain a foothold in the East Indies because Dutch merchants have allowed a certain Japanese company to lease cotton fields in Dutch New Guinea, there is actually no need to overreact. This is because the leased land is only 300 hectares, and the number of Japanese people who can work there is at most 400. (National News, 27th)

Over Forty Countries Have Implemented Sanctions Against Italy; Egypt and Persia Respond to Italian Protests

(Geneva) Experts met here today and stated that the League of Nations' sanctions against Italy are not being relaxed. The Chairman of the Sanctions Coordination Committee, Portuguese representative Vasconcelos, announced that 47 countries have banned the shipment of arms and ammunition to Italy, 43 countries have implemented financial sanctions, 37 countries have boycotted Italian goods, and 38 countries have banned the shipment of major items to Italy. In addition, many countries are either preparing to implement sanctions or have already accepted the plan in principle. It was learned today that representatives from various countries are currently considering expanding the scope of sanctions as soon as possible to include items such as oil, coal, iron, and steel. (National News, 27th)

Cairo, Egypt: The Council of Ministers has recently issued an order prohibiting the import of all Italian goods into Egyptian territory and prohibiting the transport of manganese ore and livestock to Italy. However, cotton is still permitted to be transported to Italy. In addition, the Council of Ministers has also decided to respond to Italy's protest against sanctions and will send the reply to the Italian government immediately. (Havas, 27th)

Tehran, Iran: The Iranian government has submitted a reply to the Italian protest against sanctions and delivered it to the Italian envoy to Iran today. The reply stated that the Iranian government regrets that it has had to adopt the resolutions of the League of Nations. However, the good relations between Iran and Italy still exist, and it is hoped that the current efforts of various countries will be sufficient to promote the restoration of world peace and justice. (Havas, 27th)

Italian Troops Retreat Simultaneously on the Northern and Southern Fronts; Deeply Concerned That Rear Communications Will Be Severed; Arrawe to Attack Italian Somaliland; New Italian Commander-in-Chief Arrives in Eritrea

Addis Ababa: Today, the Abyssinian authorities announced that Italian troops have abandoned Magal. After the news was released, tens of thousands of people filled the streets, cheering and celebrating. Many said that the Italians have now realized they have bitten off more than they can chew. According to government sources, the Italian troops stationed in Magal suddenly and hurriedly retreated yesterday, carrying tanks, artillery, military supplies, and heavy vehicles, gathering at the station and heading back to Adigrat, near the Eritrean border (50 miles from Magal). According to a captured native officer, the Italian troops had to retreat urgently because they had advanced too quickly, failing to clear the surrounding area, including Lantanbian, and ensure the stability of their communication lines before attacking. (Reuters, 27th)

Addis Ababa: It was officially announced here today that 1,000 Italian white troops have retreated from Magal to Adigrat, abandoning the front line for 53 kilometers. However, Askari troops are still stationed there. Abyssinians were extremely excited after hearing this news and believe that the Italian troops retreated because "clearing the countryside" was unsuccessful, so they had no choice but to retreat to consolidate their front closer to Italian Eritrea. An official in the Abyssinian palace, referring to the news announced yesterday of the Italian withdrawal from Gorahei and Galogobi, said that the Emperor's claim that the Abyssinian army could defeat the Italian army was indeed well-founded, and that Rome's claim that the Ogaden province had surrendered to Italy had been proven inaccurate. According to Abyssinian sources, if the facts are true, then Italy has returned to the position of November 23 last year, i.e., the boundary line set by the demarcation commission in Walwal. (National News, 27th)

Harar: The troops under the command of General Tafari on the southern front have invaded Italian Somaliland and are now seriously threatening the Italian communication lines. According to news today, the vanguard of the Abyssinian army, the troops of the Fano tribe, are approaching the important Italian town of Ischia Baidoa in Somaliland, which is only 150 miles from the capital of Somaliland, Mogadishu. It is reported that the main force of the Abyssinian army is not far northwest of the vanguard. According to reliable sources, this extraordinary general (Tafari) rode a white horse and led a crowd of about 100,000 from the Sidamo tribe straight down the Juba River valley, then crossed the border and entered Italian Somaliland. Although many died in battle or from fever along the way, this army advanced like a giant snake, finally reaching enemy territory and shaking Mogadishu. As a result, Italian General Graziani had to divide his troops from the Gota highlands to resist them. (Reuters, 27th)

Asmara: The newly appointed Commander-in-Chief of the Italian East African Forces, General Badoglio, arrived in Massawa this morning and will soon arrive here. (Reuters, 28th)

(Rome) Authorities here today denied the Abyssinian claim of a great victory and the Italian abandonment of Magal, calling it a joke and saying that there is no need to deny such obviously fabricated news. Furthermore, the Italian troops in Abyssinia are still firmly holding the positions they have captured. (Reuters, 27th)

Reasons for the Italian Retreat

Addis Ababa: Our special correspondent O’Chana reports that official circles here are skeptical of the claim that Italian troops are attacking the Lake Tana area. However, the simultaneous retreat of Italian troops on the Ogaden area of the southern front and the Tigray province of the northern front has attracted significant attention here. Military personnel investigating the true motives for the Italian retreat mostly say that it is because the Abyssinian army on the Tigray province front is intercepting Italian troops erratically, and the Italian army is deeply concerned that communication between the rear and the front will be severed by the Abyssinian army, so they had no choice but to retreat. As for the Italian troops on the Ogaden front, they feared that General Dejazmach Destas's troops would outflank their rear or intercept the left flank of the Italian army, so they also had no choice but to retreat. As for general speculation, it is believed that after the new commander of the Italian front, General Badoglio, arrives at the front, the strategy will definitely change. Currently, the Abyssinian army is concentrating its forces on the line from Jijiga to Dagahbur. (Havas, 27th)

Abyssinian King Removes a Political Enemy

(Rome) The deposed Abyssinian Emperor Lij Iyasu recently died in custody. It is rumored that he was poisoned by drinking poisonous milk, causing chronic poisoning. According to a war correspondent accompanying troops on the Tigray province front, when Lij Iyasu was detained in the Abyssinian capital, his former subordinates planned to escape from prison. Later, when the Italo-Abyssinian war broke out, Lij Iyasu was moved to three or four different detention locations for fear of accidents. Now that Lij Iyasu is dead, the Abyssinian King has lost a political enemy, and his position has naturally been strengthened. (Havas, 27th)

Naval Conference Next Month; Britain to Submit Proposals; Emphasis on Both Qualitative and Quantitative Restrictions

(London) It was learned here today that after the Naval Conference opens on December 6, Britain intends to submit a strong request to abolish submarine restrictions on battleship size and cannon caliber. British representatives will also propose that major naval powers exchange warship construction plans for the next six years and determine the maximum tonnage of warships of all classes. Britain advocates using this as the basis for a new naval treaty. (National News, 27th)

Britain and the United States Secretly Cooperating

(Tokyo) Noteworthy news has emerged from Japan that Britain and the United States have recently been engaged in secret negotiations and have agreed to cooperate with each other. That is, at the upcoming formal disarmament conference, Britain will disregard Japan's proposed equal ratio and fully support the US position in order to suppress Japan's new demands. They have also agreed not to propose any further reductions in battleships. On the Geneva front, the US government is secretly supporting Britain's policy toward Italy, so that Britain can fulfill its original intention of using the League of Nations to sanction Italy. Therefore, the US government is disregarding the formal naval conference, while on the other hand, it will try to put forward a new proposal to maintain peace in Europe in order to curry favor with Britain, hoping that Britain can help the US restrain Japan's attitude on the naval conference and East Asian issues. This secret cooperation plan has attracted great attention from the Japanese government. (China United Press, 28th)

Britain Asks League of Nations to Send Observers

(London) The British government intends to ask the League of Nations to send observers to attend the Naval Conference. It has sent telegrams to the governments of Japan and the United States to seek their consent. Although the replies from those countries have not yet arrived, official sources believe that they will definitely agree. (Havas, 28th)

Japanese General Nagano to Stay Briefly in Berlin

(Berlin) The Japanese Chief Delegate to the London Naval Conference, General Nagano, and his entourage of 15 people will arrive here from Moscow on Saturday. They are scheduled to stay here for one day. (Note: The conference of Japanese military attachés in Europe is scheduled to be held in Berlin on that day). (Havas, 28th)

Pacific Situation; Determining Future Policy

(Washington) The East African War has made the US government pay more attention to the Pacific. Americans are well aware that the major commercial and policy issues of the future lie in the Pacific. The US fleet's presence on the Pacific coast indicates that if the international balance of power is shaken, the US will devote all its efforts to the Pacific rather than the Atlantic. The government has repeatedly hoped to implement its good neighbor policy in the Pacific. The National Anti-War Association also supports this proposal. Grand Gathering in London - Tens of Thousands Throng the Streets - Eager to See the Preview of Our Country's Antiquities - Important Figures from Britain and Other Countries Attend Together - Viewers Praised the Rare Treasures - Will Have a Great Impact on British Art

(London) The preview of the International Exhibition of Chinese Art was held today. Many important figures from Britain and other countries attended, and there were many guests. Hundreds of cars were parked on the roadside, causing extreme traffic congestion. Home Secretary Simon and his wife waited outside the venue before the doors opened and only entered with the crowd more than half an hour later. Almost the entire London diplomatic community spent most of the day at the venue. Lord President of the Council MacDonald arrived early with his daughter and only left in the afternoon. Prime Minister Baldwin and his wife also spent several hours at the venue. British nobles and important figures from London society came together, but there were too many visitors to appreciate the exhibits carefully. Foreign Secretary Hoare and others arrived a little late and did not have time to see everything, so they all said they would come again another day. Government officials, such as the Overseas Trade Secretary and the Under-Secretary of State for India, as well as the Bishop of London and the Poet Laureate, were among the visitors.

The jade exhibition room aroused great interest, and the tiny characters engraved on the gemstone flakes, which could only be read with a magnifying glass, were especially appreciated. One room with a carved lacquer ceiling, a Ming Dynasty carved lacquer table inlaid with gold and silver threads, and a screen and large vase placed daily, was crowded with visitors. A box sent by Soviet Russia for display, containing various Chinese gold ornaments such as rings, hairpins, and bracelets, was especially noticed by women. Many viewers seemed to find the Chinese paintings hanging in the venue incomprehensible, but members of the Royal Academy of Arts of Britain studied them intently. One member said privately, "This is what I have been seeking day and night. I feel I have wasted my life." Many scholars are trying to conduct long-term research work at the venue. One scholar has been studying ancient bronzes from before the Common Era for three weeks and has not yet visited other exhibition rooms.

Today, visitors all praised the exquisite beauty of the antiquities and the thoughtful arrangement. The general opinion is that at a time when the artistic conception of Britain needs new supplements, this exhibition will have a great impact on the artistic conception of Britain. The Royal Central Asian Society of Britain will hold a reception on December 2nd, at which Guo Taiqi and the famous British scholar Pinyang will give speeches. The British government also plans to hold a banquet on December 3rd, chaired by the Minister of Works Gore, and members of the cabinet, diplomats stationed in Britain, and important Chinese figures will all attend. (Reuters telegram, 27th)

(London) The London Exhibition of Chinese Art will continue to be open to the public until it closes in March next year. This Exhibition of Chinese Art is hosted by the Royal Academy of Arts of Britain and is of grand scale, unprecedented in previous exhibitions. Even the Exhibition of Chinese Art held in Berlin in 1929 is far inferior. The exhibits this time were collected with unprecedented effort from all sides, displaying Chinese art from the past 3,500 years for viewing. Since the beginning of 1924, experts from Chinese art and hygiene groups here have organized study groups to go to the Far East to select and collect art treasures and negotiate with local people to transport China's priceless treasures to Britain for exhibition. Fortunately, with the support of the British government and the cooperation of the Chinese authorities, it was possible to collect all of China's most precious works of art, the essence of which is especially the treasures collected in the Forbidden City in Beijing. It is known that only a few famous officials and dignitaries have been able to feast their eyes on the treasures of the Forbidden City until recently, so their preciousness is evident.

Because the collection of Chinese art this time is so vast, the cruiser Suffolk was specially dispatched to transport it to Britain. In addition to the treasures of the Forbidden City, the exhibits on display at the exhibition also include the collections of famous collectors in Europe and the United States, which are displayed together, especially the collections of Buckingham Palace and private treasures, which add to the splendor.

After these treasures were transported to Britain, those in charge of the exhibition affairs were also very careful in the procedures such as unpacking and arranging them to avoid damage. Many experts in Chinese antiquities came to Britain to participate in the preparatory work. Only Chinese experts were allowed to enter the antique arrangement and window display. These windows were all locked in a special way. The preparatory members had carefully arranged each exhibition room, compiled an extremely noteworthy catalog, and invited various experts familiar with Chinese art to hold lectures to facilitate British and foreign audiences. The exhibits on display at the venue included carvings, paintings, porcelain, jade, bronzes, etc., a dazzling array of beautiful things, and all kinds of antiquities were full of vitality, which were all obtained from direct observation of life. (Havas telegram, 28th)

Zhangzhou Prefecture Rice Tax - Decision to Start Collecting Next Month - Representatives from Various Places Petition to Exempt Tax, Rice Merchants Unanimously Suspend Distribution of Rice for Export

Xiamen Correspondence: People from various parts of Southern Fujian previously petitioned the provincial government to exempt the collection of the Zhangzhou Prefecture rice tax, but the provincial government has not yet approved it. At 2 PM on the 25th of this month, more than a dozen representatives from the Longxi Shima Haicheng Chamber of Commerce and farmers jointly went to Zhangzhou to meet with the Director of the Tax Bureau to request a postponement of the rice tax. The Director of the Tax Bureau stated that he dared not disobey the orders of his superiors and agreed to start collecting the tax on the first day of next month. Thereupon, the representatives returned in disappointment. At the same time, the Rice Tax Office issued a notice on the implementation of the rice tax, stating: "According to the order of the Fujian Provincial Government Finance Office No. 1999, with the confidential order No. 4743 of the Provincial Government Secretariat, the 61st meeting of the Provincial Government Committee on October 30 this year resolved to prepare rice donations to offset security expenses in order to abolish the collection of various county group fee surcharges. In addition to ordering the Administrative Inspector of the Fifth District and the county magistrates of Zhangzhou Prefecture to assist earnestly and issue a notice, copy the original resolution and order immediate compliance, report the collection date, etc. This Director should comply and implement, in addition to setting up offices for inspection and verification in Shima, Shimei, Port, and Fuhe, etc., starting from the 25th of this month, according to the donation rate in the original proposal, Zhangzhou's export rice is 230 pounds, converted to the new standard weight of 211 catties, and five dimes of ocean is collected, which all should comply."

It is found that the Shima Tax Office is attached to the Che Lu Tou Tax Inspection Office, and the original plan was to start collecting on the 25th. As a result of the petitions to the Tax Bureau by representatives from various places, only a postponement to the first day of next month was granted. The Shima Rice Industry Association immediately convened a meeting on the 25th, attended by more than 30 rice merchants. After discussion, it was decided that from the 26th, all rice merchants would unanimously suspend the distribution of rice for export and stop purchasing from rural areas for ten days to wait for a resolution. After ten days, another meeting will be convened, and rice merchants in Zhangzhou Haicheng have also expressed their views. (November 27th)

Guangdong Province Issues Short-Term Treasury Bills for the Third Time - Total Issuance of 10 Million Yuan, Provincial Bank Increases Issuance of Vouchers

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangdong Province is imitating the central government in implementing the new currency policy, but without adequate preparation beforehand, the small banknotes and legal tender issued by the provincial and municipal banks are insufficient. Even the silver dollar notes printed previously have been used as small banknotes and legal tender, and those bringing silver to the bank to exchange for banknotes are still overcrowded. In recent days, the provincial bank has restricted those exchanging for banknotes, but it is still difficult to cope with the demand. Therefore, special vouchers have been issued. Local bank drafts are issued at branch offices and business offices in various prefectures, and legal tender vouchers are issued at the Guangzhou head office, divided into 50 yuan, 200 yuan, 300 yuan, 500 yuan, and 1,000 yuan denominations. It is also stipulated that for those exchanging large amounts of silver for legal tender, vouchers will be issued together at the time of payment. In addition to allowing taxpayers to use 50 yuan silver dollar legal tender vouchers or various legal tender notes for all taxes under 100 yuan, all taxes above 100 yuan should be paid with vouchers issued by the provincial and municipal banks to facilitate circulation. Recently, the Department of Finance issued treasury bills for the third time, with a total issuance of 10 million yuan, which will be issued starting on the first day of next month. The regulations for these treasury bills are as follows: Article 1: The Guangdong Provincial Government, in order to regulate finance, issues short-term treasury bills, named the "Guangdong Province Third Short-Term Financial Treasury Bills of the Republic of China, Year 24." Article 2: The total amount of these treasury bills is set at 10 million yuan in Guangdong Province's legal tender. Article 3: These treasury bills are guaranteed by the provincial treasury's income from the special tax on miscellaneous items of imported agricultural products and the business deed tax from the entire province. Counting from the date of issuance, the issuance period is 20 days. After the issuance period expires, the lottery will begin in two months, and the principal and interest will be repaid evenly over three months. Article 4: The interest rate on these treasury bills is 1% per month, calculated monthly based on the order of the lottery. That is, 1 yuan of interest is paid per 100 yuan for the first month's lottery, 2 yuan of interest is paid per 100 yuan for the second month's lottery, and so on. Article 5: From the third month after the expiration of the issuance period of these treasury bills to the date of the lottery in the fifth month, the Department of Finance will allocate the amount of principal and interest due for that month from the income from the special tax on imported agricultural products and the business deed tax and hand it over to the Guangdong Provincial Bank for safekeeping to be used for the repayment of principal and interest after the lottery. Article 6: The issuance, promotion, repayment of principal, and payment of interest of these treasury bills shall be entrusted to the Guangdong Provincial Bank by the Department of Finance. Commercial banks and silver shops in Guangzhou City, as well as miscellaneous shops, may collect vouchers for distribution in accordance with the provisions of Article 10 of these regulations. Article 7: These treasury bills are divided into 100 yuan, 50 yuan, and 10 yuan denominations. Article 8: These treasury bills are designated as bearer bonds. Article 9: These treasury bills are scheduled to be issued on December 1, 1935. Article 10: The Guangdong Provincial Bank will issue these treasury bills at 94% of the face value. Distributing firms will receive 100 yuan of vouchers for every 94 yuan of legal tender per 100 yuan of face value. Of the six yuan deducted, two yuan is stipulated as the distributing fee for distributing firms, and the remaining four yuan belongs to the voucher purchaser, that is, it is stipulated that voucher purchasers purchase vouchers from distributing firms at 96% of the face value. Article 10: Voucher purchasers or distributing firms may freely mortgage, buy, and sell these treasury bills from the date of issuance to the date of the last month's lottery and may also use them as security deposits or guarantees for other public affairs. Article 12: Those who forge these treasury bills or damage credit and other acts will be punished according to law. Article 13: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation (November 23rd)

Fujian Province Tobacco Label Proceeding - Tobacco Prohibition Associations Established in Various Counties One After Another - Annual Sales of Local Opium in the Province Approximately 6 Million Yuan

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Fujian Provincial Tobacco Prohibition Committee was organized and established in September. The counties that have reported the establishment of branch associations include Minhou, Changle, Ningde, Nanping, Gutian, Yong'an, Shunchang, Pucheng, Jianyang, Songxi, Zhenghe, Shaowu, Hui'an, Anxi, Zhangpu, Dehua, Haicheng, Longyan, Zhangping, Shanghang, Jianning, Tong'an, Jinjiang, Zhao'an, Luoyuan, Fuding, Minqing, Putian, Nan'an, Changtai, Ningyang, and other counties. The remaining counties are being urged to organize by the Provincial Tobacco Prohibition Committee in conjunction with the Department of Civil Affairs, with a deadline of the end of the year for uniform establishment. The association plans to eradicate opium throughout the province within three years. The first step is to register opium addicts, and the second step is to establish opium addiction treatment centers, each with a term of six months. The first term is for voluntary registration and voluntary opium cessation, and the second term is for compulsory registration and compulsory opium cessation. For each county branch association that has been established, the provincial capital sends one investigator to handle the registration of seedling varieties and opium addicts. These investigators are publicly selected and recruited, trained for three weeks, and taught various opium prohibition regulations before being sent to serve in various counties. The first batch of more than 20 people has completed training and has been dispatched recently. The second batch has also begun training. Recently, the Provincial Tobacco Prohibition Committee also resolved that the local opium paste companies in various counties should be managed by the county government to prevent the theft and sale of private opium. Opium paste shops are not allowed to sell opium paste to unregistered opium addicts. Although opium addicts have been registered, they should also smoke at home and not gather to smoke in opium dens. In addition, each county is ordered to report the situation of opium addict registration on a monthly basis for verification. For those that have been completed, each county district should obtain a certificate of guarantee and submit it for review. If there are any inaccuracies, the county magistrate and district chief should be severely punished. As for the situation of opium paste sales in various counties of the province, according to the latest report from the Opium Prohibition Supervisory Office, a large county such as Jinjiang can sell 12,000 taels per month, and a small county such as Zhangpu can sell 2,000 taels per month. The price of each tael of opium is approximately 3 yuan. Jinjiang should sell more than 400,000 yuan annually, and Zhangpu should sell more than 70,000 yuan annually. If the average annual sales of opium in each county, large or small, is standardized at 100,000 yuan, then the more than 60 counties in the province should sell more than 6 million yuan of opium paste, which can be said to be huge. However, Zhao Dajun, Director of the Opium Prohibition Office, still believes that the party, government, and military organs in various places have failed to understand the tasks of the opium paste companies and shops, resulting in many obstacles to the process and making it difficult to handle. The tax revenue has not improved. He went to Hankou this month to report the situation to the head office and requested resignation. After being retained by the head office, in addition to urging him to actively proceed with methods to promote sales, he also sent a letter to the provincial government ordering its subordinates to assist in handling the matter. Another person, Feng Wenyu, was appointed as Deputy Director to assist in planning. Zhao and Feng both arrived in the province yesterday. There may be some changes to the province's future methods for promoting opium sales. (November 27th)

Beiping: Financial Situation Increasingly Chaotic - Merchants Worry and Unwilling to Accept Central Government Dime Notes - Difficult to Exchange Copper Yuan Tickets for Bus Rides and Purchases - Tianjin Issued New Copper Yuan Tickets with a Reserve of 200,000 Yuan

Beiping Correspondence: Due to Tongzhou's declaration of autonomy, the market in Beiping feels more depressed, and the financial sector is even more unstable. In addition, due to the disturbances of the Tianjin Autonomy Daredevil Team, copper coins are increasingly being hoarded, resulting in the suffering of not being able to exchange paper money for copper coins. Many small private banks and cigarette shops are hoarding copper coins and are unwilling to exchange them. The authorities have not been able to negotiate concrete and effective measures to crack down on this. Stores in Dong'an Market, Xidan Market, and Quanye Market, as well as ordinary vendors, are unwilling to accept dime notes and copper yuan tickets, and even dime notes are not welcome. Trams are also unwilling to accept paper tickets. Citizens are suffering from not being able to exchange them and can only cry in despair. The chaos in the financial sector has reached this point. Although the Beiping municipal authorities intend to thoroughly resolve this, they intend to change the standard price of copper coins to 500 to 470 coins per yuan, that is, 5,000 to 4,700 wen, as in Shanghai, so that there is room for flexibility, but a decision has not yet been made to implement this.

In fact, there is no shortage of copper coins in Beiping. Because the market price is lower, most hoarding merchants are unwilling to sell them. The hoarding of steel coins is quite complex. Tram companies and tea, oil, and salt shops are hoarding the copper coins they receive in small amounts. Farmers, servants, and footmen also try to collect and save small amounts of copper coins when they see that steel coins are scarce. Although the amount saved by each person is limited, the number of savers is large, so the quantity is naturally not small. Because the supply of steel coins cannot meet the demand, prices have risen sharply, but the casting of new copper coins is not allowed by the authorities, so the only option is to issue new copper yuan tickets to facilitate market circulation, and the price of copper coins will naturally fall, and the accumulated copper coins will flow out.

In order to rescue the copper yuan, the Beiping financial community organized the Hebei Province Copper Yuan Ticket Issuance Reserve. The internal organization consists of six directors, appointed by Zou Quansun, Ji Hua, Zhou Zuomin, Zhong E, Yao Zesheng, Wang Xiaoyan, and others. The Hebei Provincial Government and the Pingjin Municipal Governments will each appoint one supervisor. The reserve fund is tentatively set at 200,000 yuan, which will be raised by groups such as the Pingjin Chambers of Commerce, banks, and silver coin guilds. The expenses will be met from the interest generated by the reserve fund. If it is not enough, the Hebei Provincial Government and the Pingjin Municipal Governments will be asked to subsidize it. The scope of work is to rescue finance and circulate the market, and it does not engage in profit-making businesses. In order to meet urgent needs, the old copper yuan tickets stored but not yet issued by the Hebei Provincial Bank in Tianjin will be used temporarily, totaling approximately 300,000 yuan. After new tickets are printed, they will be gradually withdrawn. During the period of substitute use, the ticket face will be stamped with a small seal of the "Hebei Provincial Bank Copper Yuan Ticket Issuance Reserve." This has been approved by the last meeting and entrusted to Zhou Zuomin to be fully responsible. It is expected that it will be realized in the shortest possible time. (26th)

A Brief History of the Development of Modern Science (A Lecture to National Middle School Students on November 16th and 18th)

— (Continued)

(II) Reasons for the Rapid Advance of Modern Science

Modern science history begins with Columbus's discovery of America, as mentioned earlier. Not long after the discovery of the New World, the Portuguese Magellan and others circumnavigated the globe, proving the theory of a spherical Earth, which greatly invigorated the thinking of Europeans. Besides this, there are five other reasons for the rapid advance of modern science, which are detailed below.

I. The Renaissance - The period from the 14th to the 16th centuries was the European Renaissance, its greatest achievement being "the awakening of mankind." This means: "I have ears and eyes and cannot abandon intelligence; I have a brain and cannot abandon thought; I have a conscience and cannot abandon judgment." Not only is the development of scientific research a manifestation of this spirit, but also the outbreak of the religious revolution and the emergence of vernacular literature were influenced by this spirit.

II. The Establishment of the Scientific Method - According to archaeological estimates, our planet has existed for about 250 million years, and human history for about one million years. Why has science not progressed as rapidly in this long period of one million years as it has in the last one or two hundred years? This is because the scientific method was only fully established at the beginning of the 17th century. The Englishman Bacon and the Frenchman Descartes opposed the prevailing deductive method and advocated the inductive method. Bacon's book "New Organon" elaborates on the meaning of the inductive method. He said that we should first observe natural things in order to find principles; we should not rely solely on subjective reason and force all facts to fit. Bacon's inductive method has three steps: (1) collect all facts without omission; (2) analyze and compare all facts; (3) discover the causes of each phenomenon. I will give another example to illustrate the application of this method: someone sees bubbles in a pond getting larger as they rise from the bottom and asks why the volume of the gas increases. To solve this problem, the first step is to collect all the facts about changes in gas volume; the second step is to analyze and compare, thereby discovering that both pressure and temperature can change the volume of a gas; the third step is to assume that the distance between gas molecules can change, and then use experimental methods to prove whether this assumption is correct. Thus, the conclusion is reached: the distance between gas molecules can be changed by external pressure; the pressure of the water in the pond is greater at the bottom and smaller at the top, so the bubbles gradually increase in volume as they rise from the bottom. This conclusion is based on many observations and experiments, and has undergone rigorous criticism and comparison, so it is more reliable. Descartes' method went further; he advocated first dividing a problem into the simplest factors, and then using Bacon's method to conduct scientific research on each factor. The methods of Bacon and Descartes were indeed important tools for the development of science.

III. The Development of the Experimental Spirit - The scientific method must be based on precise observation and experimentation, otherwise the conclusions are unreliable. For example, the great Greek philosopher Aristotle said, "When two objects are dropped from above, the heavier one falls faster and the lighter one falls slower." According to general observation, this conclusion seems to be correct, and it is said that for more than two thousand years no one could point out his error, until Galileo used the height of the Leaning Tower of Pisa in the 17th century to drop two iron balls, one weighing one hundred pounds and the other weighing one pound, at the same time, proving that light and heavy objects fall at the same time, and the speed is not related to weight. The experiment itself is very simple, and its fame does not lie in being able to correct Aristotle's error. This experiment demonstrates the greatness of Galileo's experimental spirit. Before, when Galileo discovered the three laws of falling bodies, everyone thought they were inconsistent with Aristotle's theory and denounced them as absurd. Galileo dared to disregard the accusations of the public and led the crowd to conduct the "Leaning Tower Experiment." His experimental spirit was truly great. Because of his scientific views, he was subjected to various persecutions by the church at the time, but his aspirations and views never changed. Later generations called him the ancestor of modern science because of his research and experimental spirit.

IV. The Establishment of Universities and Academic Societies - Universities provide an environment for academic research, and academic societies provide members with opportunities to learn from each other. Both can promote the development of science. At the beginning of the modern period, universities in various European countries were already established. At that time, great scientists such as Copernicus, Kepler, Bacon, Galileo, Newton, etc. all received university education and worked in universities or their research institutions. Universities encouraged scientific research, so science was able to advance rapidly. European academic societies originated in Naples, Italy. This was the first scientific society in the West, founded in 1560. The first scientific society in England was founded in 1645, and the first scientific society in France was founded in 1666. Now, academic societies are established in various countries and are an important factor in promoting science. Academic societies are even more important than universities, because when academic societies hold meetings, each member first presents the research results, and then everyone discusses them, debating and asking questions, which often arouses everyone's interest in research, and sometimes can point out the direction of a person's research or correct his mistakes. The combination of academic societies and universities has created an excellent scientific environment and a strong atmosphere for scientific research.

V. The Invention of Printing and the Flourishing of Scientific Books and Newspapers! - Before the invention of printing, books were mostly copied or carved on stone or wood, and were expensive and difficult for ordinary people to buy. Since the German invented movable type in 1445, more than ten thousand books have been published in Europe in just a few years, which naturally has a great relationship with the progress of science. By the middle of the 17th century, scientists gradually felt the need to communicate with each other, so various academic societies published scientific periodicals. Scientific journals were published in France and England in 1665 at the same time. Scientific journals have three purposes: (1) to publish various research records and reports, so that others can use them as reference when studying the same problem; (2) to communicate with each other to avoid the drawbacks of duplication; (3) to encourage individual research and promote benign competition among scientists. Someone said, "Generally, it takes ten years for a scientific invention to be used as middle school teaching material, but important inventions are published in the newspaper on the same day, and are recorded in magazines within a month or two at most." This statement has considerable reason, so I would like to ask all middle school students to read newspapers and scientific magazines in addition to textbooks, because the progress of science now is definitely something that textbooks cannot keep up with.

The above five reasons are very important. I will give an analogy to help you remember. Science is like the advancement of a train; the Renaissance is like the railway, enabling the train to advance boldly and vigorously; the scientific method is like the locomotive, giving the train the ability to advance; the experimental spirit is like coal, which is the driving force of the train; research institutions and academic societies are like the train itself, carrying many scientists; magazines and publications are like signals, such as traffic lights, indicating the route the train should take. These five conditions were only fully met after one hundred and fifty years, and since then science has been advancing rapidly on the track towards a bright future.

Changzhou: Hai Prefecture Refugees Rob Rice

At Yutai Rice Store in the north entrance of Taiping Lane, Xi Dou Wai, Wuyi County, at around 9:00 a.m. on the 27th, sixty to seventy refugees from Haizhou who had walked to Changzhou from Xinmin Town suddenly arrived. First, seven or eight men went to the store under the pretext of buying rice, followed by more than twenty women who crowded into the store and poured rice into the cloth bags they carried, taking away three or four dou of white rice in total. The station immediately dispatched Police Chief Yin to lead the police to suppress the situation. However, the women who robbed the rice had already fled far away. Nantong: Protecting Sailing Vessels During the Winter Defense Period

In order to ensure the safety of sailing vessels, the county government has formulated measures for winter vessel protection. All ships passing through townships and stopping are inspected by the military and police. During the winter defense period, remote small ports are closed and navigation is suspended. Regardless of the size of the vessel, no vessel may stop or embark/disembark passengers within the county's boundaries except at designated ports.

Zhejiang Province Fishermen's Loan: Both Parties Agree on Principles; Total Amount is 150,000 Yuan, Borrowed by Six Banks; Contract May Be Signed After Further Consultation

Regarding the loan for fishermen in Zhejiang Province, after Xu Qingfu, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance, wrote to Zhang Shenzhi, Director of the Shanghai Ningbo Fellow Townsmen Association, to continue discussions with six banks, including the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Siming Bank, China Industrial Bank, and Zhejiang Local Bank, the following four principles have been decided: (1) The banks will lend to the fish wharves in Shenjiamen. (2) The ratio of loans from the fish wharves and the six banks will be determined with the loans from the fish wharves acting as guarantee for the loans from the six banks. (3) When repaying the loan, the loans from the six banks should be repaid first, then the loans from the fish wharves. (4) The total loan amount is 150,000 yuan, with a monthly interest rate of 2%. After final consultation on the above principles, the contract can be formally signed.

Sanbei Company's River Steamer: Changxing Stranded in Zhenjiang; Hengshan Already Heading to Rescue

Sanbei Company received a telegram yesterday afternoon from the Yangtze River steamer Changxing, stating that it was stranded above Zhenjiang and had taken on water. The company is currently sending a vessel to rescue it. The details are as follows:

Encountered Fog En Route

The Changxing vessel has a large capacity and many passenger seats, making it a leading first-class ship among the company's Yangtze River vessels. Captain Jia Dingxiu has a deep reputation and is a senior veteran among Chinese pilots. He has a long tenure and can always turn danger into safety. On Tuesday night of this week at 2 a.m., the vessel departed from Shanghai, sailing upstream to Wuhan, fully loaded with cargo.

Vessel Stranded

After midnight on the 27th, the vessel was traveling above Zhenjiang, near Twelve Fort, at a place called Shihyeh Chow. Due to the heavy fog and rain at that late hour, the river pilot mistakenly navigated to shallow waters, causing the vessel to run aground. The captain measured the waterline on the starboard side and found that the vessel's heavy cargo caused it to sit deep in the water. He planned to try to dislodge the vessel himself at high tide, as there is a difference of seven to twelve feet between high and low tide.

Reported to Shanghai by Telegram

Two hours after running aground, Captain Jia attempted to reverse at full speed to free the vessel. However, water was discovered in the engine room, making self-rescue impossible. Yesterday afternoon, two telegrams were sent to Shanghai, reporting the situation of the Changxing's grounding and the flooding of the vessel.

Hengshan Heading to Rescue

The Changxing vessel departed from Shanghai carrying over 11,000 pieces of cargo and a significant number of passengers bound for Wuhan. Passengers panicked after the grounding. Yesterday afternoon at 5 p.m., another telegram was received from Captain Zheng stating that the company's Hengshan vessel was passing through the area and had been requested to assist in the rescue. If it can be rescued, that would be best. If the rescue is unsuccessful, other measures will be considered, such as unloading the cargo from the vessel.

Pilots Association Strives: Prioritize Hiring Chinese Crew; Break the Habit of Preferring Foreign Crew; Request the Navigation Bureau to Enforce

The Chinese Merchant Marine Pilots Association has petitioned the Ministry of Communications to instruct the Navigation Bureau to enforce the prioritization of hiring Chinese crew members to help unemployed Chinese crew. The full text of the petition is as follows: "Petition for the enforcement of prioritizing the employment of Chinese crew members for the sake of many unemployed national crew members. It is requested that an order be issued not to be deceived by foreigners. We have found that since China opened its seas, we have had to rely on talent from other countries due to the lack of navigational expertise. This led to the loss of maritime rights, which was a painful but necessary measure at the time. Fortunately, in recent years, the country has spared no effort in cultivating navigational talent. According to the current statistics of Chinese crew members, there are enough to serve Chinese merchant vessels, and there is no need to rely on foreigners. Some shipping companies do support Chinese crew members, but many still prefer to hire foreign crew members, leading to a significant number of unemployed Chinese crew members. In order to provide relief, our association has petitioned your ministry to instruct the Navigation Bureau to order all shipping companies to prioritize hiring Chinese crew members when recruiting crew members. Your ministry approved this petition and instructed all companies to comply. The companies should strictly abide by the ministry's order to create job opportunities for Chinese crew members. However, we have recently discovered that some shipping companies, such as the Northern Shipping Company's Beihang vessel, hired a foreign first mate to replace another who was transferred. The Shanghai Navigation Bureau informed them of the ministry's order and demanded compliance, ordering them to dismiss the foreign first mate and quickly hire a Chinese replacement. The company was forced to comply with the law. However, we have recently heard that the foreign first mate, holding a valid first mate certificate, claims that he should have the right to perform his duties and that the Shanghai Navigation Bureau should not refuse to clear him, and will appeal to your ministry. We believe that the Navigation Bureau, given the large number of unemployed Chinese crew members, should prioritize hiring Chinese nationals when the company recruits crew members, as a means of providing relief, and should not refuse clearance to the foreign crew member. This is a legitimate action that both upholds the law and helps unemployed Chinese crew members. Our association is deeply concerned that your ministry will listen to only one side of the story and be deceived by the foreigner. If this happens, not only will the Navigation Bureau find it difficult to enforce the law in the future, but the number of unemployed Chinese crew members will increase. Furthermore, the Northern Shipping Company has always been dominated by foreign crew members. If we do not fight for it this time and allow the company to hire another foreign crew member, it is feared that Chinese crew members will never find employment with that company. Therefore, we urgently petition your ministry to order the Navigation Bureau to enforce the law of prioritizing the employment of Chinese crew members. If foreigners file complaints, please investigate carefully and not be deceived. This will be a great virtue."

Social Bureau: Regulates Silver Dime Exchange Rate; Yesterday Ordered the Chamber of Commerce and the Banking Association to Discuss and Report

The Municipal Social Bureau, upon receiving a petition from the Civil Federation of the First Special District of the city to restrict the exchange rate of silver dimes, issued orders to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Banking Association yesterday: "According to the report submitted by the Civil Federation of the First Special District of this city, 'Since the Ministry of Finance promulgated the reform of the currency system on the third of this month, the market was temporarily chaotic at the beginning, but it quickly returned to normal. However, unscrupulous merchants have been engaging in selfish activities, and there have been rumors of buying silver-content coins, resulting in extremely disparate exchange rates on the market, ranging from the regulated rate of twelve dimes to less than eleven dimes, and sometimes even ten dimes and three hundred cash. As the use of legal tender begins, people's hearts are initially stabilized, but unscrupulous merchants dare to create such a fraudulent market to disrupt people's hearts, which should be strictly prohibited. We hereby submit this report to your bureau, requesting that you, together with the Public Security Bureau, etc., strictly investigate and arrest these fraudsters to restore order. We respectfully submit this to the Shanghai Social Bureau for your consideration.'" According to this, the report is indeed true. This matter concerns finance and should be strictly investigated. In addition to issuing orders, we hereby order your association to promptly discuss and report with the local banking association and the local chamber of commerce so that we may review and handle this matter. This order is issued."

Beijing-Shanghai Railway: Derailment Locomotive Repaired

The derailment of a freight train locomotive on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway at Hushu Pass Station the night before last has been reported in various newspapers. The true story of the derailment, as investigated, is continued below. According to reports, at 9:20 p.m. the night before last (the 27th), after freight train No. 503 on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway arrived at Hushu Pass Station, locomotive No. B-46 was detached and driven from the bend to the east end of the station's siding, then reversed back onto the main track in preparation for towing other vehicles. Unexpectedly, while the single locomotive was reversing onto the main track, two large wheels and the water tank car wheels derailed simultaneously, blocking the track. The railway promptly dispatched rescue trains from Changzhou and Shangbei to provide assistance. At 2:20 a.m., all the derailed wheels were returned to the track, and the entire line was operating normally after 3:00 a.m. Due to the derailment, passenger trains No. 3 and No. 80 arrived at the scene of the accident. To avoid excessive delays, the railway asked the passengers of those two trains to exchange carriages and head back to their destinations separately. Passenger trains No. 5 and No. 6 were also slightly delayed due to meeting traffic.
