Famine Refugees Sell Children: Westerner Appeals on Their Behalf

Yesterday, a Westerner submitted the following letter to this newspaper for translation and publication: "Returning home on Sunday evening, walking west on Difeng Road near St. George's, I saw two men and two women next to a stone wall. Each woman held a baby. As I approached, the two men spoke in a northern dialect, saying 'Selling children,' shouting it two or three times. The plaintive sound pierced my heart and will never be forgotten. I hope that readers who are sleeping soundly in their warm beds at night can also hear it. I asked them where they came from and learned that they were all honest farmers from the north, who had fled to Shanghai due to the drought and famine. Unfortunately, although Shanghai is prosperous, it is also frighteningly indifferent. They had no relatives or friends and their meager savings were quickly exhausted. Therefore, they had no choice but to sell one of their children in order to get a few days' worth of food to survive. I gave them all the money I had in my pockets so they could buy food to eat, and then asked for help from the patrolman at the intersection. He said there was no place for them. I then asked the New Royal Hotel for assistance, hoping to find some spare space where the suffering people could find shelter from the wind and frost, but they refused, saying there was no room. I then consulted with the Salvation Army, which has hostels for foreigners and shelters for released prisoners, but does not accept honest farmers fleeing from famine. I then pleaded with one of China's largest churches, but they also closed their doors. Finally, I inquired with the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, who treated me with courtesy, but also said they could not accommodate refugees arriving in Shanghai. Alas, where can these hungry crows roost? Or why are they being rejected by everyone?"

Jianghai Customs Announcement to the Public Regarding Antiquities Exports Requiring Submission for Verification, Education and Interior Ministries Jointly Issuing Passports: Announcement: By order of the Ministry of Finance, the circulation of antiquities is limited to domestic use. The Civil Federation of the First Special District of this city sent a document to the Municipal Government yesterday, titled "Petition to Stop the Price Increase of Raw Materials." Shipping Industry to Increase Cargo Fees by 20% Starting January 1st Next Year: Due to Increased Prices of Hardware and Coal

The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association received instructions from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which had been forwarded by the Social Bureau, prohibiting price increases during the government's currency policy implementation, and requiring them to submit proposed reasonable prices to the bureau for record-keeping. The Shipping Industry Association responded that the member companies are currently facing higher operating costs due to rising prices and have requested the association to review the situation. This matter was submitted to the 37th Executive Committee meeting on the 22nd of this month for discussion. The committee members agreed that the value of ships has increased and the prices of hardware, materials, machinery, and iron plates have soared due to exchange rate issues. Other essential items such as coal have also increased in price. All expenses have increased significantly compared to the past. At a time when the shipping industry is declining, this sudden increase in burden makes it difficult to sustain operations. If no remedies are taken, it will be difficult to maintain the status quo. The only source of income for shipping companies is cargo fees. Since expenses have increased, they must find ways to compensate from the income side to survive. Shipping expenses are like the cost of goods. When the cost of goods increases, the price naturally follows. This is a matter of common sense and should not be compared with speculative attempts to deliberately raise prices. In this environment, shipping companies have no choice but to increase cargo fees to some extent to make up the difference. It was decided to increase cargo fees by 20% on all routes starting on January 1, 1936. This decision has been reported separately to the Social Bureau and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for record-keeping.

Banking Industry Decides to Repay Loans from Commercial Banks by the End of the Month: After the End of the Month, They Will Repay Loans from the Three Banks

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Ministry of Finance previously established the Banking Industry Supervision Committee to provide relief to the banking industry, allocating 25 million yuan in the form of 1935 national financial bonds. The Banking Industry Reserve was responsible for 3 million yuan, and various commercial banks were responsible for 4 million yuan each. The Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications jointly assumed 18 million yuan. The banking industry was able to weather the crisis. The loans have long since expired. The Banking Industry Reserve has repaid the 3 million yuan. Most of the 4 million yuan from the commercial banks have been repaid. The borrowing pawnshops plan to completely repay the loans from the commercial banks by the end of this month. As for the 18 million yuan from the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, they will find a way to repay it after the end of the month. These loans are all secured by collateral, such as deeds, treasury bills, and valuable warehouse receipts.

After reports that Fujian Province was planning to impose a special tax on incense, candles, and firecrackers at a rate of 30%, the Local Firecracker Industry Association immediately telegraphed the Fujian Provincial Government, requesting that firecrackers, as hygiene products, be exempt from the tax, and also telegraphed the Ministry of Finance requesting a ban on the tax. Please be informed."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Instructs: Questions on Stamp Duty for Partnership Contracts

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday replied to Baokang Pawnshop with instructions on the method of affixing stamps to partnership contracts. The reply stated, "We received your letter of inquiry regarding the affixing of stamps to contracts on the 27th of this month. The answers are as follows: (1) If A and B each contribute 6,000 yuan, according to Article 16, Item 18 of the Stamp Tax Law, and the notes in the remarks column, each should affix stamps based on the amount of capital they contributed, which is 1.20 yuan each. If C, D, E, F, G, and H each contribute 3,000 yuan, each should affix stamps according to the above standard, which is 0.60 yuan each. (2) According to Article 3 of the Implementing Rules of the Stamp Tax Law, 'The copies and transcripts mentioned in Item 7 of Article 3 of the Stamp Tax Law are limited to those that are completely identical in content to the original with the affixed stamp duty, used only for verification purposes and not for use.' In your letter, the eight shareholders each hold a copy of the contract, which is stamped. The other copy is held by the manager, who does not have any shares. The manager does not hold this as proof of rights, but only for verification purposes. Therefore, this is a copy as referred to in Article 3 of the Implementing Rules and does not need to be stamped. However, the word 'copy' should be noted on the contract to avoid confusion by the inspectors."

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: New River Steamer Bidding Opened Yesterday: Resumption of Yangtze River Service Temporarily Difficult

According to Guowen News Agency, the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company plans to use the surplus of 45,000 pounds from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund to build two river steamers. The board of directors decided to build two river steamers similar in design to the Taikoo Company's Wusong steamer. The company drafted all the plans for the ship's length, width, design, and cargo capacity and submitted them to the Ministry of Communications, which forwarded them to the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Board of Directors for approval. The materials and machinery will be purchased from the United Kingdom, while the ship's hull will be built in China through open bidding. After the public bidding process began last month, the bidding for one of the ships was officially opened yesterday. The construction cost is approximately 800,000 yuan, and construction should be completed within one year. The decision for the other ship will be made by the board of directors. Regarding the company's resumption of Yangtze River service, a spokesperson for the company stated yesterday that there are no current preparations for this. Furthermore, the extensive repairs to the Emei ship have not yet been completed, and there is no way to predict when the service will resume.

Domestic and Foreign Wireless Telephone to Open; Ministry of Communications Orders Shanghai Telegraph Bureau to Improve Long-Distance Lines

The Daily News reports that the Ministry of Communications yesterday instructed the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, stating, "The international and domestic wireless telephone services planned by this Ministry are about to open for business. The construction of long-distance telephone trunk lines connecting various provinces is underway and will soon be completed in stages. To ensure clear communication, the urban telephone lines connected to the aforementioned wireless telephones and long-distance trunk lines must be improved to meet the telephone circuit transmission standards promulgated by this Ministry. After investigation, it has been found that the resistance of the supervisory signal coils within the cord circuits of small exchanges installed by long-distance telephone users is generally low, resulting in very low impedance, which is detrimental to long-distance communication. Each such case should be inspected, and those with the aforementioned circumstances must have their supervisory signal coils replaced, or one pair in the cord circuit can be modified into a straight-through type specifically for long-distance communication. Furthermore, the telephones used by users to connect to domestic and foreign wireless telephones and national long-distance trunk lines are of great importance to the volume of communication and should also be carefully selected and inspected from time to time to ensure they are suitable for long-distance communication. You are hereby instructed to comply and implement the above. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau, Jinan Bureau, and Hangzhou Bureau are to separately notify the Shanghai Telephone Company, Jinan Telephone Company, and Zhejiang Provincial Telephone Bureau to comply accordingly and report on the implementation status. Minister Zhu Jia驊."

Nine Acres; Counterfeit Opium Manufacturing Ring Busted; Three Members of Liu Family Involved

Recently, someone secretly set up a manufacturing ring for counterfeit opium at No. 14 Luxiangyuan Road, Nine Acres, Nanshi. The counterfeit raw materials are made by roasting paste soil and opium ash together. They work day and night, extremely busy, and after they are made, they are distributed to various places, passing them off as high-grade opium. Unexpectedly, the matter was discovered by the detective team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Chief Captain Ji immediately ordered Sha Daxin, the captain of the Fourth Detachment, to lead a large number of detectives to the house the day before yesterday evening, where they seized more than 100 catties of counterfeit opium, opium ash, copper opium pipes, account books, and other evidence. The three main culprits, Liu Fenlan, Liu Jiyao, and Liu Da, were arrested and taken back to the detachment. Detectives are now being dispatched for thorough investigation, pending transfer to the bureau for interrogation.

Li Jinbiao Crushed to Death by Machine

Li Jinbiao, a native of Hubei, 32 years old, had been working at the Shengli Steel Window Factory at No. 284 Liuying Road, Xibaoxing Road, Zhabei. At 10:30 a.m. yesterday, Li Jinbiao was working carelessly when his clothes were suddenly caught in the belt of a machine. Da Fu Lane Morphine Ring; Liu Zhiming Acquitted After Appeal

Inspector Jin Jiulin, detective Zhang Ziying of the French Concession Police, and other detectives from the shift, busted a morphine manufacturing ring at No. 7 Da Fu Lane, Maggie Road, on the afternoon of September 29th. They arrested four people, including Li Asheng, Cai Henian, and his brothers Gu Jiahao and Zhou Xinlai, all from Pudong. They then went to No. 7 Sanyu Lane, Lafayette Road, and arrested Liu Zhiming from Ningbo, recognizing Liu as a shareholder of the ring. Ten bottles of alcohol and two bottles of hydrochloric acid were found in his home. They were sent to the Special District Second Court for prosecution. At the conclusion of the trial, Cai Asheng and the other five people were sentenced to imprisonment, and the morphine manufacturing machinery, equipment, and raw materials were confiscated. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Now, Liu Zhiming, dissatisfied with the original judgment, hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Hua Maosheng to present reasons for appealing to the High Court's Third Branch. The reasons stated that the confiscated alcohol and hydrochloric acid were sent to his home by his friend Wang Yonghe, and he had no stake in the ring. The High Court's Third Branch specially convened a collegial panel last Saturday to summon and interrogate him. At the conclusion of the trial, yesterday afternoon, the acting presiding judge Sun Honglin, accompanied by Judges Wang and Xiong, and Prosecutor Dong, arrived at the Criminal Court No. 3 to announce the verdict. The portion of the original judgment concerning Liu Zhiming's guilt was overturned. Liu Zhiming was innocent. After the announcement, Liu requested bail, and the court ordered him to submit a written request for approval.

Municipal Bureau of Education; Convenes Biao Biao Opera Actors for Training; More Than 30 Actors Including Bai Yushuang Attend; Section Chief Jiang Instructs on Areas for Improvement

The Municipal Bureau of Education, recognizing that the Biao Biao operas performed by Bai Yushuang and others at the Empire Theatre and the North China Opera Theatre are obscene, has been sending personnel to review them daily, banning or censoring them separately. Yesterday, it specially convened all the actors for training at 10:00 a.m. in the lecture hall of the Citizens' Education Center. The details are as follows:

Attendees: Including Section Chief Jiang Jianbai of the Municipal Bureau of Education, Lei Kenan of the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, Lu Hailan, Yuan Zengyu, Ding Shoutang, and Sun Yucai of the Opera and Record Review Committee, and actors Bai Yushuang, Chen Peigen, Guo Yunfang, Wang Shaolun, Xian Lingzhi, Ai Lianjun, Wang Baolan, Sai Lingfa, Xiao Yufeng, Li Guiqin, Ya Lijun, Zhang Xiangzhong, Mao Enqiang, Zhao Yueting, and others, more than 30 people.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Cai, Section Chief, began by stating, "The Municipal Bureau of Education has convened everyone here today, hoping that after this conversation, there will be improvements. Shanghai is a place where people from all over gather, with a dense population. Various entertainment groups have been organized and guided by the Bureau of Education from time to time. However, there are not many Biao Biao opera performers, so there has been no opportunity to talk. The Bureau of Education has sent personnel to review, and they feel that the content and review standards are quite inconsistent. It should be strictly banned, but considering the livelihood of the actors, we are giving them an opportunity to improve. We know that drama today is no longer as despised by the general public as it used to be. Drama is social education. The strength or weakness of a country depends entirely on education. China's weakness and stagnation are due to the lack of widespread education. To popularize education, we rely on school education on the one hand and social education on the other. To ensure that all social dynamics contain good educational meaning, the general public will be educated through what they see and hear. Drama is even more widespread education and can influence countless audiences. Therefore, in terms of performance, we must pay close attention and not allow the audience to become depressed or extreme as a result of watching the play. We must be able to give the audience a good effect. The drama review standards prohibit anything that violates the Three Principles of the People, loses the national image, harms public safety or morals, or promotes superstition, heresies, or feudal ideology. There is a lot of obscenity in Biao Biao opera. We hope that you will pay attention to the singing, dialogue, expressions, and movements, and also improve the script. You are all teachers of the people. We hope to work with educators to be good social teachers, whose power is even greater than that of elementary school teachers."

Review Opinions: Next, Lei Kenan, a representative of the Bureau of Social Affairs, gave a speech, hoping that actors would improve their knowledge to improve themselves. Then, Lu Hailan, a member of the Opera and Record Review Committee, reported on the review opinions and the areas that should be improved: (1) In terms of tone, do not have obscene puns; (2) In terms of tone, do not have decadent music; (3) Do not have obscene movements; (4) Horror plots, such as killing children for revenge, are prohibited; (5) Actors should not have behaviors that seduce the audience; (6) The insertion of other elements should not be overly exaggerated. If you can do these points, you can get on the right track.

Representative's Response: Finally, Wang Shaolun, a representative of the actors, gave a speech, stating, "Today, we are grateful for the invitation and training by the Municipal Bureau of Education, and we accept and thank you for your instructions. Biao Biao opera has been performed in Shanghai for a year. This opera is most popular in Tanggu and Jinzhou in the north, and it is done by two or three people playing the basin drum in a grass band. It is very low-class. Therefore, the two groups performing in Shanghai this time are no longer Biao Biao opera. It is the same status as Ping opera and Ping opera, but the erhu and bangzi are slightly different. However, in order to cater to the psychology of the general public, the name is still used. Because the plot of this play is very old, there are many things that do not fit the times. We hope that you will guide us to improve it."

Ningbo Bank Recovery Rumors; Creditor Sues; Demands Repayment of Deposits; Defendant Hopes to Settle

Wu Zhihao, a wealthy businessman from Ningbo, previously founded the Ningbo Industrial Bank on Nanjing Road in Shanghai. Due to financial difficulties, it announced its closure on June 5th of this year. It is currently preparing to resume operations. According to the recovery plan, creditors will be repaid 20% in cash first, 30% will be a two-year term deposit, and the remaining 50% will be used as the bank's capital after it resumes operations. Seven out of ten creditors have agreed. Now, 51 creditors, including Gu Jiating, have jointly hired lawyers Chen Kunyuan and Liu Yan to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against the bank's directors Wu Zhihao, He Shaoting, Yu Guozhen, Wang Boyuan, Zeng Guohua, Wu Zhihe, Chen Cuifu, Dong Zhongxiu, Yang Songren, Zhuo Yuting, Sun Yihan, Xiang Shengwu, Zhou Yongsheng, He Shaoyu, Lin Kanghou, and supervisors Zhuang Songfu, Guo Yonglan, Yuan Duanfu, and Lu Qisheng, totaling 19 people. The object of their claim is divided into two parts: (1) A ruling that the Ningbo Industrial Bank's assets should be liquidated to repay the 43 plaintiffs' savings deposits of 11,698 yuan and 6 jiao. If this is not enough to repay the outstanding deposits, the 19 defendants should be jointly and severally liable for the repayment; (2) The Ningbo Industrial Bank's assets should be liquidated to repay the 11 plaintiffs' current deposits of 1,574 yuan, 3 jiao, and 7 fen, and they should bear their litigation costs separately. According to Article 15 of the Savings Bank Law, the directors and supervisors should be jointly and severally liable for the repayment. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Daxi of the First Special Court convened a hearing in Civil Court No. 13. Only four defendants, Wu Zhihao, Wang Boyuan, Xiang Shengwu, and Lin Kanghou, arrived with lawyers Yu Hualong, Zheng Wenbang, and Wu Baotai. First, the plaintiff's lawyer stated the reasons for the lawsuit and requested a default judgment against the defendants who did not appear. The defense lawyer for Wu Zhihao stated that the Ningbo Industrial Bank has been approved by the Ministry of Finance to resume operations, and seven out of ten creditors have signed subscription agreements. Shao Quan, one of the plaintiffs in this case, has already received the deposit and returned the deposit certificate. Zhou Xiangguang and Wu Peigao, also plaintiffs, have agreed to the recovery plan and signed the subscription agreement. Some of the plaintiffs have also settled. Therefore, this case should be settled. The lawyers for Lin Kanghou and Xiang Shengwu denied that Lin and Xiang were directors of the bank. The court, considering that this case still requires investigation and summoning the plaintiffs, adjourned the case to be heard again at a later date.

French Concession: Car Theft Ring Cracked; Four Criminals Sentenced

The French police, led by Detective Xu Kai (transliteration), Chinese Detective Zhou Ruzhang, and Officer Peng Zhengyou, recently cracked a ring specializing in the theft of rickshaws (referred to as "pulling yellow oxen" in their jargon). They arrested Zhili An, a Jiangbei native responsible for the thefts, and Zhou Chuanfa, who managed transportation. In a house at 167 Haig Road, which served as their base, they recovered five stolen rickshaws. They then apprehended Zhao Yongnian and Shen Weiqing, who were guarding the stolen goods.

Taken to the police station, Zhili An and others confessed that Liu Wenkui (aka Xiao Wuzi) and Zhao Kaisi were the ringleaders, that Rong Tiancai was responsible for contacting rickshaw owners to negotiate ransom, and that Tang Xiaoshunzi, Yang Tiancheng, and others posed as passengers to plan thefts.

The detectives went to arrest Liu and the other five, but they had caught wind of the operation and fled. Therefore, Zhili An, Zhou Chuanfa, Zhao Yongnian, and Shen Weiqing were presented along with twelve victims to the Second Special Court, where public prosecution was initiated according to law. Judge Li Changnian held a court hearing to investigate the situation. The details have already been recorded in this newspaper.

The interrogation in this case has now concluded. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Li presided over the first criminal court and sentenced Zhi Anli to three years in prison for habitual theft. Zhou Chuanfa, a repeat offender of theft, was sentenced to two years and six months. Zhao Yongnian and Shen Weiqing were each sentenced to four months for harboring stolen goods. Shen Weiqing received a two-year suspended sentence. During the appeal period, Shen Weiqing was allowed to be released on bail, while the others were returned to the detention center to await transfer to prison after the appeal period. Since this cracking down and punishment of thieves, this trend can be curbed, and rickshaw owners can enjoy a period of peace.

University Student Sentenced for Abusing Servant Boy; Combined Sentence of One Year and Two Months

Zhong Qichang, a twenty-three-year-old student from Pinghu, Zhejiang, residing at 36 Shikang Lane, Avenue Joffre, French Concession, bought Lai Fa, the son of his neighbor Qing A'long, in his hometown two years ago as a servant for seventeen yuan. He brought him to Shanghai and forced him to do adult work. He also made him serve Zhong's opium smoking every night until 2:00 or 3:00 AM before he could sleep.

If Lai Fa was careless in his work or dozed off at night, he would be whipped and abused in every way, making the child's life unbearable. His body was covered in wounds, a truly inhumane situation. The second landlord advised Zhong to stop, but to no avail. On the 15th of this month at 2:00 AM, Zhong severely beat Lai Fa again, causing swelling and injuries to his head and body. The second landlord, who was actually French police officer Li Liansheng, reported it to the French police, who arrested Zhong. A search uncovered weapons such as rattan canes and wooden sticks, as well as opium paraphernalia. Lai Fa was taken into custody.

The Legal Affairs Office of the Police Department initiated public prosecution on charges of restricting freedom, enslavement, assault, and opium use, according to the criminal law. Criminal Court President Wang Gangxu conducted a thorough investigation and set a date for sentencing. The details have been reported in previous issues. Yesterday was the sentencing date. At 10:00 AM, Judge Li Changnian presided over the first criminal court and ordered the defendant to be brought to the stand. Zhong Qichang was sentenced to six months imprisonment for abusing a male under the age of sixteen and hindering his natural physical development, one year imprisonment for enslavement, and a fine of sixty yuan for opium use. He was given a combined sentence of one year and two months imprisonment. The fine was included in the execution of his sentence. The charge of assault was not accepted. If the fine is converted to labor, it will be at a rate of two yuan per day. Lai Fa was permitted to be adopted by Pan Jishi (Lai Fa's biological older brother), who provided a guarantee. If no guarantee is provided, he would be sent to the Xin Pu Yu Tang orphanage.

During the appeal period, the defendant was held in the detention center. His defense lawyer requested bail. After deliberation, the court granted bail upon payment of five thousand yuan and a guarantee to appear whenever summoned.

Counterfeit Currency Dealers Arrested; Three Defendants Remanded for Further Interrogation Tomorrow

Chen Deshan, a native of Henan, and Cheng Daosheng, a native of Anhui, were in the business of selling counterfeit currency. The other day, Chen and Cheng went to the Taihexiang Cigarette and Paper Shop at 354 Avenue Edward VII to peddle counterfeit money. The shop feigned interest, and they agreed on a price of thirty-four yuan in silver for every hundred yuan of new counterfeit notes from the Bank of China. However, due to the greater ease of using older counterfeit notes, the price was raised by one yuan, making the price thirty-five yuan per hundred yuan. The delivery was scheduled for the previous evening.

Unfortunately, the plan was leaked to Chief Inspector Feng Zhiming and Detective Wu Hanzhang of the Inspectorate General. The two officers, along with French Inspector Brett, waited outside the Taihexiang Cigarette and Paper Shop around 8:00 PM the previous evening. Soon enough, Chen and Cheng arrived and were whispering to each other nearby. They were apprehended by the officers. Thirty new counterfeit one-yuan notes from the Bank of China were found on Chen, and one new and one old counterfeit one-yuan note were found on Cheng. They then went to 141 Zhifu Road and apprehended another accomplice, Zhang Churong, a native of Anhui, and found another counterfeit one-yuan note on him. All three were taken to the Xinzha Police Station and detained.

Yesterday morning, Legal Advisor Zhang Tianyin of the Police Department presented the case to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court, charging them with counterfeiting currency in violation of Article 196 of the Criminal Law. Chen Deshan confessed that the counterfeit money was given to him by Hou Cuixi, who is at large, at Pingjiang Lane in Ximen, who asked Cheng to find a way to sell it. Cheng Daosheng also admitted to peddling the money to Taihexiang. Zhang Churong claimed that the counterfeit one-yuan note found on him was given to him by Chen.

Judge Liu Yugui reviewed the confessions and ordered the three defendants remanded in custody for further interrogation on the 30th of this month.

Our association will find a house for them and negotiate their relocation. We also request that your bureau send personnel to contact the troops to facilitate the matter, as the Chao Hui Shanzhuang has a larger building, which can accommodate over three thousand people. At this time of financial difficulty, rather than establishing multiple shelters and spending more, it is better to combine them into one place, which is more economical. Therefore, it is necessary for the security troops to relocate. The reception period is expected to begin around December 10th. If the weather turns cold suddenly, it will be advanced at any time. Now we are preparing all the necessary matters. As for the reception expenses, each charitable organization will donate at the meeting on the 21st, totaling over eleven thousand yuan. However, based on past years' expenditures, at least twenty thousand yuan is needed. This year the number of people to be accommodated will definitely increase, and expenses will definitely increase. The amount donated by each charitable organization is far from enough, and fundraising is extremely difficult. The city government has allocated three thousand yuan each year. The difficult situation this year is even worse than in previous years. We earnestly request your bureau to forward a request to the city government to allocate an additional two thousand yuan in addition to the usual three thousand yuan. Any additional amount will be raised by our association to cope with the situation. In addition to notifying you of the scheduled reception, we respectfully reply and request your review and processing.

The Municipal Public Security Bureau believes that there are a large number of tailor shops in the city, and there are quite a few that operate properly. However, a small number of shops take advantage of the low costs and run away with valuable clothing materials from customers, causing losses to customers. As for the registration of employment agencies, the bureau has distributed application forms to the sub-bureaus and police stations, instructing them to distribute them to the employment agencies in their respective jurisdictions to fill out. Registration will begin next month. After the application forms have been submitted and reviewed, those that are found to be upstanding will be granted a business license. Those that are not up to code will be eliminated.

Representatives of each factory, including Lu Hongbin, Huang Kechang, and Ni Hanru, were led by General Representative Wang Zhisheng and Secretary Li Qiaozhi, and departed from Shanghai on September 17th.

After the fair closed on October 16th, representatives of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce of the embankment of Saigon, French Indochina, contacted General Representative Wang and requested that he travel to Saigon to participate in the Chinese National Products Exhibition hosted by the chamber. They then traveled to participate. The exhibition opened on the 7th of this month and closed on the 14th.

Successive Returns to Shanghai

After the Saigon exhibition, the representatives returned to Shanghai in batches. The first batch included Lu Damin (Shenghuo Textile Factory), Chen Guibei (Zhongxing Trading Company), and Wu Yousheng (Yaguang Manufacturing Company). The second batch included Wang Zhisheng (General Representative), Li Qiaozhi (Secretary), Yang Zhongkang (Zhongda Machine-Made Leather Goods Factory), Ni Hanru (Southern Industrial Cooperative), Liu Derun (Huaxing Hat Factory), Yang Xihe (Haijing Woolen Mill), and Lu Hongbin (Zhongxin Factory). The third batch, including Huang Kechang and Zhu Qinhuai (Taikang Food Company), arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday.

Patriotism of Overseas Chinese

This morning, the reporter made a special trip to interview Mr. Huang Kechang, representative of Taikang Company. According to him, this was the first time that manufacturers of national products had traveled to Nanyang as an entire group to hold an exhibition. When the manufacturer representatives arrived in Singapore, they were warmly welcomed by the local overseas Chinese. On the first day of the opening of the fair, over 50,000 people attended. People from remote areas even came by carriage to attend the grand event. During the fair, it rained occasionally, but the spectacle was not diminished. The goods shipped by each factory were sold out. For example, the goods shipped by our company, worth about six thousand yuan, were all sold out. Upon returning to Shanghai, we received orders totaling over eighty thousand yuan. The patriotism of the overseas Chinese in Nanyang to support domestic goods is unparalleled. Each factory has now appointed an agent in Nanyang to specialize in sales and accept orders.

Hongqiao Sanatorium Reduces the Burden on Patients; Room Rates and All Fees Reduced to Very Low Levels

Hongqiao Sanatorium at 201 Hongqiao Road in western Shanghai is known for its complete facilities. Since Dr. Yan Fuqing has been working hard to rectify it, the interior has been completely renewed. All departments are staffed by specialist doctors specially hired by Dr. Yan. The tuberculosis and X-ray departments are headed by Dr. Su Shihai, a German medical doctor. All the rooms in the hospital have recently been repainted. In view of the dire economic situation in society, the hospital has revised its inpatient regulations, and all fees have been reduced to very low levels. In particular, the rooms that were previously 20 yuan a day have been reduced to 12 yuan, and the medium-priced rooms have been reduced to 4 yuan, 3 yuan, and 2 yuan, so that patients, regardless of their economic situation, can afford to seek medical treatment, with the aim of making it more accessible and reducing the burden on patients. Therefore, the number of patients at the hospital has suddenly increased in recent days. It is reported that a certain well-known person is also receiving treatment at the hospital.

Regulations for Parking Locations Near the Great Shanghai Theatre

Article 29 of the Public Works Department's Traffic Regulations will be amended with the following provisions, starting on December 2nd of this year, prescribing regulations for parking and driving around the Great Shanghai Theatre.

Vehicles dropping off and picking up audience members at the Great Shanghai Theatre must travel south. Vehicles parked on Baker Road west of Tibet Road must park on the north side of the road. Vehicles parked on Baker Road east of Tibet Road must park on the south side of the road. Vehicles parked on Tibet Road north of Baker Road must park on the east side of the road. Vehicles parked on Lloyd Road south and north of Baker Road must park on the west side of the road. After the show, vehicles picking up passengers and proceeding must travel south.

Also, starting on that day, the time for parking vehicles on Tibet Road between Nanjing Road and Baker Road will be limited to between 12:00 AM and 2:00 PM the following day. The provisions of Section 2 of Article 47 of the Traffic Regulations will also be amended accordingly.

Fortunately, Ju's mother was alive and provided occasional relief. However, because she was not tolerated by her parents-in-law, Ju temporarily returned to her mother's home. Later, through the mediation of friends, Chen Gensheng agreed to pay Ju and her two children ten yuan per month for living expenses. Unexpectedly, after only a few months, he stopped the payments, resulting in a significant accumulation of debt. Furthermore, during Xianzhang's illness, medical expenses and business losses led to urgent demands from creditors. Ju borrowed 800 yuan from Mr. Li to repay the debts. However, when the loan came due, she had no money, leading to legal pressure. In this situation, Ju had no choice but to hire lawyer Feng Song to file a lawsuit in the First Court's civil division against her father-in-law, Chen Gensheng, requesting an order for support. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wang Wenkui presided over the hearing in the Seventh Civil Court. The defendant did not appear, and lawyer Zhou Xiaoan appeared to defend him. Lawyer Feng Song, representing the plaintiff, stated that the plaintiff, Chen Ju, is currently 28 years old. She requests support payments from this year until she reaches 60 years of age, at ten yuan per month, as well as the 800 yuan debt, and the assumption of legal costs. Judge Wang reviewed the case and announced that the case would be scheduled for a hearing at a later date.

A Visit to the China Wool Spinning Factory

— Wu Yuxuan

The manufacture of woolen yarn is one of the departments of the wool textile industry. Therefore, the manufacture of woolen yarn has not yet received attention. As a result, the various woolen yarns used daily are almost entirely supplied by foreign goods in industrialized countries such as Europe, America, and Japan. According to customs records, the average annual import amount has been more than six million gold units in the past three years, which has invisibly become a major loophole in my country's national economy. In recent years, the voice of saving the country through industry has risen, and people with lofty ideals have begun to set up their own factories to imitate foreign goods to remedy this loss. The first domestic manufacturers engaged in this business were the Dongya Xianghe two factories in Tianjin, and the Zhenxing, Zhanghua, and San factories in Shanghai. However, these factories mostly operate woolen yarn manufacturing as a sideline to their main production business. In addition, the British Jardine Matheson Spinning Mill and the Japanese Shanghai Spinning Mill also operate this business as a side business. Since last autumn, the Shanghai Wool Textile Factory, Yumin Textile Company, and China Wool Textile Factory have been established one after another. At the same time, the British Baldwin Knitting Yarn Factory, which was once famous in the Chinese market for its Bee Brand woolen yarn, also set up a factory in China this spring to avoid high taxes from the Chinese government and facilitate competition. As a result, the woolen yarn manufacturing industry has become one of my country's emerging industries. To understand the content of this emerging industry, the reporter visited the recently established China Wool Spinning Factory on November 21 with the industrial and commercial visiting group of this newspaper.

The China Wool and Velvet Textile Factory is located on Linqing Road in Yangshupu. The person in charge is Mr. Chen Wuqin, the manager of the factory. When the reporter and others arrived at the factory, Mr. Chen and Associate Manager Bi Zhongying warmly welcomed them. First, they introduced the establishment of the factory. According to them, the preparation for visiting the factory, which has been developing vigorously for nearly forty years, is to introduce the establishment of the factory. However, my country's hundred industries are backward. To this day, people can only sigh that the textile industry can compete with foreign goods. In June of last year, the person in charge once went to Japan to inspect the woolen yarn manufacturing business to learn from it. However, most of Japan's industries are kept secret, so the results of the first inspection only revealed that Japan's woolen yarn textile industry uses French machines and the general situation of Australian wool. It was not until the second inspection that they could slightly know the inside story. After returning to China, they immediately raised a capital of 250,000 yuan, ordered machines from the French Desheng Foreign Company, hired French technicians, and at the same time selected a site and rented a house. By September of this year, the machines were finally installed, and the factory was officially put into production. From June of last year to September of this year, the preparation period lasted for more than a year, and the machine installation took about four months. The factory's capital has actually expanded to hundreds of thousands of yuan.

After Mr. Chen and Mr. Bi briefly described the establishment of the factory, they immediately led the reporter and others to inspect the factory for a week. The factory's building is divided into three parts. The first part is the woolen yarn weaving workshop, which has eight drawing machines, five spindle machines, one carding machine, and one joining machine. The work of the eight drawing machines is collectively called the front section. The first, second, and third drawing machines each have four functions at the same time: (1) lengthening, (2) thinning, (3) removing dirt, and (4) combing evenly. After the raw material wool tops (semi-finished products of raw wool) pass through the first, second, and third drawing machines, they gradually become thin, long, even, and clean yarns. In addition to having the same functions as the above three drawing machines, the fourth drawing machine also has a softening function. This machine is the latest invention. Most of the wool spinning factories that have been established for a long time do not have this equipment. Its selling price is about 19,000 yuan in national currency per machine. The fifth, sixth, seventh, and eighth drawing machines only have two functions: lengthening and softening. Because the dirt removal and uniform scooping of the yarns after passing through the first four drawing machines have been completed, the work of the last four drawing machines is determined by the thickness of the required yarn and the number of drawing machines it should pass through. After the drawing work is completed, the manufacturing process immediately turns to the back spinning section. The back spinning includes the work of three machines: spindle machines, joining machines, and carding machines. First, the yarns that have passed through the spinning work are sent to the spindle machine to make them into yarn bobbins. Then, the yarns on the bobbins are passed through the joining machine to become twisted woolen yarns. Finally, they are passed through the carding machine to become bundled woolen yarns. (To be continued)

Education News

Ministry of Education Supervisor Zhong's Inspection: Zhejiang Provincial Vocational Education Report (3)

9. Private Wu Ling Elementary Vocational School: This school was established with donations from Mr. Chiang Kai-shek. It has four elementary classes with ninety students. Fourth-year students focus on practical work, and are assigned to various agricultural organizations for apprenticeships, divided into four groups: Agricultural Economics, Agricultural Technology, Rural Education, and Agricultural Extension. The intention is commendable. It has over two hundred acres of farmland, not including the forest area. It is divided into four sections: crop cultivation, horticulture, animal husbandry, and extension. It has achieved some success in selecting seeds and raising livestock. Teaching emphasizes self-study, encouraging students to read carefully instead of relying solely on lectures. Assessments are also rigorous.

Due to many teachers returning to their hometowns during the vacation, the school cannot implement vacation assignments. The school should provide dormitories for teachers' families to prevent all teachers from leaving the school, leaving the farm without responsible guidance. The school buildings are very beautiful, but may not be suitable for the living conditions of agricultural students to cultivate adaptability to the environment. To ensure the school's facilities are complete, a girls' vocational class should be added, focusing on education in home economics and rural household handicrafts. The affiliated elementary school has both male and female students, but the elementary agricultural department only admits boys, depriving girls of educational opportunities, which is a great pity.

10. Provincial Jin Tang Normal School Elementary Agricultural Science Department: This department has two elementary classes with forty-two students. Recently, due to the small number of applicants and the susceptibility to the influence of the normal school atmosphere in agricultural training, many graduates have also engaged in education. Therefore, enrollment has been temporarily suspended. It has one hundred and twenty acres of farmland and over thirty acres of orchards. Apart from designating certain areas of land as public practice fields for experimentation, the remaining seventy to eighty acres are leased to each student at one to two acres per student for self-cultivation, planting, and harvesting. The school is only responsible for guidance. All profits are used to subsidize student expenses, which is a very good method. Crop yields are satisfactory. The summer vacation internship lasts three weeks, with meals provided by the school. All equipment, except for modern agricultural tools, is barely adequate. However, due to teachers occupying too many rooms, the physics and chemistry lab, library, and farm tool room are all cluttered and crowded. The department could try providing one year of normal school training to elementary agricultural graduates, or emphasizing both normal school and agricultural studies, and simultaneously establishing farmer's supplementary classes, focusing on cotton seed improvement, without suspending enrollment.

11. Private Ming De Nursery Elementary Normal School with Affiliated Home Economics Vocational Department: The school has three departments: a four-year elementary normal school, a three-year ordinary home economics department, and a three-year women's ordinary supplementary department, with a total of eighty students. For the first three years, the home economics and normal school departments attend classes together. Those who wish to become teachers are instructed to study education and teaching practice for one year. The supplementary department aims to complete the entire elementary school curriculum. It should be converted into a vocational supplementary school, providing home economics training to older, unschooled women to lay the foundation for improving family life.

The school has an affiliated elementary school, kindergarten, and nursery, paying close attention to the diet and nutrition of children and infants. Some students even bring their children to study at the school, educating the children while studying themselves. Those from slightly poorer families also take care of children for others, earning seventy to eighty yuan per year to subsidize their expenses, which is a very good approach. The main goal of students coming to the school is to acquire knowledge and skills in managing a household, which aligns well with the original purpose of home economics education. Therefore, among the students are mothers and young women, making it a rare school in the country. The students range in age from sixteen or seventeen to thirty or forty, with an average age of twenty-eight. The teaching and equipment for ordinary subjects urgently need improvement, but the implementation of specialized subjects is quite good. The equipment is not yet fully complete, and there are only two specialized teachers, which should also be supplemented to ensure completeness.

12. Private Continental Senior Surveying Vocational School: The school is divided into three classes: surveying and control surveying, with approximately eighty students. The control surveying training class admits students who have completed the second year of junior high school and graduates in one year. Although the career prospects are good, their academic ability is too poor to be useful. They should be given opportunities for further study, and in the future, junior high school graduates should be admitted and given one and a half years of training.

The subjects in the senior surveying department are appropriately allocated. Specialized subjects have a teaching schedule. Most of the teachers are part-time personnel from the surveying bureau, and the teaching is considered effective. The practical training time is also sufficient. Basic exercises are conducted in the first year, concentrated practical training for six weeks each semester in the second year, and two months of practical training in the third year. The methods are quite good, and surveying instruments are also sufficient. Students' career prospects do not seem to be a problem.

13. Private Hangzhou Women's Elementary Home Economics Commercial Vocational School: The school has three elementary sewing classes, four elementary commercial classes, two ordinary supplementary classes, and one apprentice class, with a total of approximately three hundred students. Among them, the commercial department is more developed. The commercial department focuses on Chinese, English, and mathematics, all exceeding the prescribed hours. Practical training is a maximum of four hours per week per person (half in banks and half in stores). Typewriters are insufficient for practice, and there are no Chinese typewriters. Research on commodities and surveys of market conditions are both lacking. Graduates still have credibility in the financial sector. In recent years, career prospects have gradually become difficult. Of the forty recent graduates, twenty-two wish to work, while the rest plan to pursue further education or are sent to banks outside the school for practical training, which should be scheduled before graduation and considered as part of the practical training. The school's internal store has overly simple equipment and provides little benefit. After graduating from the sewing department, many serve the country, but the situation is not clear. Their work performance is quite good, but cutting skills still need more attention. The school's name includes "home economics," but the class hours for home economics subjects are very few, which should be addressed. If a separate department cannot be established, it can be attached to the sewing department. Teaching should emphasize imparting knowledge of household hygiene, parenting, and household economics. The commercial department can also pay attention to this. The ordinary supplementary class should be transformed into a supplementary class with vocational implications, providing sufficient training in life skills and housekeeping knowledge to older, unschooled women, with classes held in the afternoon and evening. The continuation of this type of education should not be judged based on the number of students, as a new facility cannot initially outperform others. The apprentice class focuses on work and has very few classes, being entirely business-oriented. Subjects should be appropriately added to align with the purpose of vocational supplementary education. Principal Ms. Xie Xue maintains the school affairs with painstaking effort. Recently, due to old age and declining strength, there is a lack of successors. She has repeatedly requested the Education Department to take over. The Education Department should consider this. If it can be taken over by the province and expanded, it would greatly benefit women's vocational education in Zhejiang.

14. Provincial Financial Personnel Training Institute: This school was originally private but recently became provincial. It currently has four classes with one hundred and sixty students, graduating in three years. All courses focus on accounting, statistics, and bookkeeping, which are very similar to senior commercial studies. It should be renamed Senior Commercial or Senior Financial Vocational School to comply with regulations. It once tried a one-year program, assigning graduates to serve in various counties, but the results were poor. Later, it recruited elementary school students to graduate in three years, but the results were also unsatisfactory. Judging from the service status of graduates, most can use what they have learned. However, all training and effectiveness are similar to the provincial senior high school commercial department. The two schools should find a way to merge to avoid duplication. First-year students have no practical training, second-year students have internal practical training, and third-year students are introduced to various financial collection agencies for apprenticeships in the second semester, which is a very good approach. Teaching management is also practical and strict.

Interpretation of Foreigners Establishing Supplementary Schools in China

(Nanjing, 28th dispatch) The Ministry of Education, based on a request from the Ping Municipality Social Bureau for an interpretation of the doubts regarding foreigners establishing public supplementary schools in China, has specifically instructed the bureau, stating that if the nature of the school involves imparting skills or lecturing on academics, targeting those who have already received education, and providing higher knowledge or skills training, it is permissible to establish such schools under guidance and supervision. However, if the purpose is to provide supplementary education for unschooled citizens or illiterate individuals, foreigners are not allowed to operate such schools.

Progress of Compulsory Education in Guangdong Province: Elementary School Students Increase by 24%, Elementary Schools Increase by 18%

Guangzhou communication, Since Guangdong Province implemented the three-year administrative plan, the progress of compulsory education has been extremely rapid. Compared with the twenty-first year, the number of elementary schools has increased by 18 percent, and the number of elementary school students has increased by 24 percent. In the twenty-fourth year, it is estimated that approximately 1,200 short-term elementary schools can be added. It is now reported that Mr. Huang Linshu, the director of the Provincial Department of Education, is currently drafting the second phase of the three-year education administrative plan, paying close attention to compulsory education. The province has had a compulsory education committee since the seventeenth year, but the organizational outline of the committee has been in place for a long time and is mostly inapplicable. It has been revised into the Organizational Regulations of the Guangdong Provincial Compulsory Education Committee, and experienced individuals from the education sector have been hired as committee members to plan and promote compulsory education. The revised regulations are excerpted below.

Organizational Regulations of the Guangdong Provincial Compulsory Education Committee: Article 1: The Guangdong Provincial Department of Education, in accordance with Article 27 of the Provisional Measures Outline for the Implementation of Compulsory Education by the Ministry of Education, establishes the Provincial Compulsory Education Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee") to assist in handling compulsory education in the province. Article 2: The main tasks of the Committee are as follows: A. Formulate a plan for promoting compulsory education in the province. B. Supervise the management and use of compulsory education funds in the province and the subsidies granted by the central government to compulsory education in the province. C. Formulate measures for training teachers in stages. D. Evaluate the performance of compulsory education in various counties and cities. Article 3: The Committee shall have the Director of the Education Department as the Chairman, and the Director of the Education Department shall hire experienced individuals from the education sector and designate several officials from the Education Department as members. Article 4: The Committee's plenary meetings shall be held once every three months, with the Chairman of the Committee as the chairman. Extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary. Article 5: When necessary, the Committee may convene representatives from the compulsory education committees of various counties and cities to discuss matters concerning compulsory education in the province. Article 6: The matters decided by the Committee and the education plans formulated shall be implemented after being approved by the Education Department and reported to higher authorities for record. Article 7: All members of the Committee shall serve in an honorary capacity. Article 8: The Committee may establish a secretariat, which shall be staffed by officials designated by the Education Department. Article 9: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation upon approval.

Establishment of the Municipal Museum Preparatory Office: Recruiting Service Staff on the 5th of Next Month

The Shanghai Municipal Museum building was designed by architect Dong Dayou and was completed in early this month. The entire building follows the latest European and American museum designs, and is magnificent, being one of the city's major buildings. It is reported that the museum's board of directors has established a preparatory office at the Zhonghua Xueyi Society on Love Lane for the convenience of preparation, and has invited the municipal government to appoint Li Dachao and Hu Zhaochun as the chief and deputy directors of the preparatory office. It has been operating since the 16th of this month. All collection methods have been printed in special booklets and distributed to all sectors to solicit publicly. The collection groups are tentatively divided into two departments: history and art. The collection methods are divided into three types: purchase, donation, and deposit. It is also reported that the museum plans to recruit several service staff on the 5th of next month and has sent letters to the principals of various famous middle schools to recommend students for registration.

Middle School Teachers' Education Research Association: First Research Meeting of the Moral Education Group; Discussing Cooperation Between Schools and Families and Improving the Health of Middle School Students

The city's Middle School Teachers' Education Research Association held its first meeting of the Moral Education and Military Training Group yesterday afternoon at 4:00 pm at the Lake Society. Shen Tilan, Shen Tongyi, Tang Zeng, Tong Xingbai, Huang Yiru, Guo Shouchun, Lin Meiyan, and Mai Foru attended. Li Pengfei from the Municipal Education Bureau was present. Shen Tilan chaired the meeting, and He Chengfu recorded the minutes. Case 8 and Case 9 on how to cultivate students' national ideology were merged. Research questions: (1) The promulgation of the National Crisis Period Training Program and Case 9 on how to cultivate students' national ideology were merged for discussion. As a result, the original proposer, Mailun Middle School, was asked to formulate a concrete plan for discussion at the next meeting. (2) The case on strengthening cooperation between families and schools. As a result, Dagong School was asked to refer to the following points to formulate methods: (A) Organizing parents' associations. (B) Reporting students' situations at school to parents in a timely manner. (C) Schools paying attention to students' lives at school at any time. (D) Organizing student college and career guidance to cooperate with parents. (3) How to improve the health of middle school students and Case 6 on whether students should adopt a separate meal system for boarding at school. As a result, the following points of view were raised and the original proposer, Jingye Middle School, was asked to supplement and reorganize them: (A) Prohibit the reading of unhealthy publications that can damage physical and mental health and the viewing of unhealthy films. (B) Promote Chinese martial arts. (C) Encourage students to participate in extracurricular activities during daily rest periods. (D) Stipulate the minimum standards for physical education equipment in each school. (E) Promote popular sports among students. (F) Check students' physical fitness. (G) Pay attention to individual student health issues. (H) Pay attention to sex education. (I) Whether or not to separate meals should be determined by each school depending on the situation, but attention must be paid to kitchen hygiene, dietary nutrition, and students with infectious diseases. Schools that have achieved good results in implementing the separate meal system can be used for reference. (4) Should military management be implemented in middle schools? and Case 10 on how educational administrative agencies should assist in the realization of military management were merged. Dagong School was asked to collect them by sending a letter. (B) Request the Education Bureau to send a letter to the National Military Training Association to strictly supervise the military instructors of each school to implement it effectively. (5) The next meeting is scheduled for December 12 at 4:00 pm at Huaging Garden.

University of Hong Kong Recruiting New Students

The University of Hong Kong will recruit new students in Shanghai in June next year. Those who wish to take the exam can obtain an application form from the university's registry, fill it out according to the format, and return it to the office before February 1. Those who pass the exam will be given an admission certificate, which can be used to formally study at the university or at famous universities in the United Kingdom such as Cambridge, Oxford, London, etc. The detailed admissions regulations are available for two silver dollars per copy and can be purchased at the Hong Li Baidang at 219 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (1)(0)(9)

—Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

At that moment, Mr. Rice, who was driving past in a cart loaded with hay, heard Mrs. Jo calling him and turned around. She wanted him to take the whole class to the meadow and pick them up at five o'clock.

"This will inevitably delay some of your work, but it doesn't matter: we're willing to reward you with blackberry pie," Mrs. Jo said, knowing Mr. Rice's weakness.

His rough, dark, and yellow face immediately lit up, and he laughed happily, "Ha! Ha! Oh, Mrs. Pei, if you first allow me this delicious thing, I will immediately obey."

Mrs. Pei was then greatly relieved and walked back into the room, saying to everyone, "Children, I have already arranged everything. You can all go." She loved to make them happy, and she felt very distressed when she occasionally disturbed the quiet life of her youngest son; because she believed that adults should give sympathetic respect to children's small hopes, plans, and pleasures, and should not rudely stop or ridicule them.

Upon hearing this, Don was overjoyed and asked, "Can I go?"

"I especially thought of you, be careful, and don't bother with the strawberries, just sit and be glad that you can often find your beloved things around you and quietly observe and enjoy them," Mrs. Pei replied, clearly remembering his kindness to her child just now.

"I'm going too! I'm going too!" Rob was extremely happy, dancing and singing, hitting the lid of the tin bucket, making a sound like cymbals.

Sports News

1935-1936 Women's Basketball Rules Changes Announced by the China National Sports Association

Chapter 3, Section A, Article 5: Both the referee and the inspector have the right to declare a "timeout." The following (2) is added to this article: The referee or inspector shall have the right to declare a "timeout." Chapter 3, Section C, Article 2 of the Inspector (4): Coaches may request the inspector to change the positions of players. The full text is changed as follows: When necessary, the inspector shall declare a "timeout" (If a coach of a certain team requests to change the position of a player during the game, the inspector shall grant the request and declare a "timeout." This timeout is treated as the same as a substitute player for that team.)

The inspector may instruct the substitute player to report to the recorder, but it is not a mandatory duty.

Chapter 4, Section C, The following section is added after Article 2 of Ball Skills:

It is illegal to resume catching a ball that has bounced on the ground more than once with one movement.

Chapter 4, Section E, Article 2 adds an explanation of "blocking" fouls. The full text is as follows:

Players may use any legal method to defend against an opponent holding the ball. If the defended player has a tendency to bump into someone, such as if the defender maintains their original defensive posture after the opponent has released the ball, then the defender has committed "blocking."

Chapter 7, Article 4: The timeout time is limited to one minute (the old rule was two minutes).

Chapter 7: The following section is added to Article 2 of free throws: The rule is two minutes.)

Chapter 9: The following section is added to Article 2 of free throws:

If a guard fouls a forward (including the center), the fouled forward shall take the free throw. If a forward fouls a guard, the free throw may be taken by any forward (including the center) player who was present at the time of the foul.

Chapter 10, Section B, Article 3: If a team has no substitutes and two or more players are disqualified, the game shall be stopped, and the outcome of such a situation shall be two to zero (as the team forfeits). The following parenthesis is added after the third sentence:

When a substitute player enters the field, they should report to the inspector, except when the game is being officiated by one official instead of a referee. The following sentence is added after the end of the section:

If a team has no substitutes and one player is disqualified, then the team can only continue the game with five players. However, if two or more players are disqualified, then the game shall be won by the opposing team. If it is a forfeiture, the result should be two to zero, otherwise the recorded score will be valid.

If a player changes positions without leaving the field, it will not be considered a substitution or change, but if the position in the field is changed, the recorder and inspector must be notified.

Chapter 10, Section C, Article 2 (2): When throwing the ball in the center circle, the time for a player to hold the ball in the center circle while waiting is limited to three seconds (the old rule was five seconds).

Chapter 11, Section A, Free Throws, the following paragraph is newly added to Article 1 (A):

When taking a free throw, the player's feet may leave the ground, but before the ball leaves their hand, their feet must not cross the free-throw line.

Yu Qing Defeats Yue Zhong in Basketball Game, Result: 37 to 17

Since the beginning of the semester, Jiangwan Yu Qing Middle School has spared no effort in promoting sports, especially basketball, where they have been invincible. Yesterday, they had a friendly match with Yuehan Affiliated High School at the school's gymnasium. Both sides faced each other, and the game began with a bang. Yuehan took the lead with 3 to 0. Yu Qing's center, Han Renxiang, unwilling to be outdone, scored several goals with skillful moves. After that, both sides traded points, but Yu Qing was ultimately one step ahead, ending the first half with a score of 20 to 12. After the break, the intense battle resumed. Yue Zhong showed a do-or-die spirit, and their two forwards were very active. However, Yu Qing's two guards defended like an iron wall, and forward Zhang Liangxiong's long shots were accurate. Yue Zhong could not maintain the situation, and the game became one-sided. As a result, Yu Qing returned in triumph with a score of 37 to 17. The lineups of both sides are recorded below:

Yu Qing Fouls Points

Forward Zhang Liangxiong 2 16

Recorder Wei Heyuedian 0 4

Wang Jincheng 0 5

Securities Securities Transaction Over 65 Million Yuan Bond Discounts at 92 Highest, 75 Lowest

Transaction Volume Yesterday, November 28th, was the settlement date for the November futures of the Chinese Securities Exchange. The market was closed the day before (November 27th) to prepare for the settlement. This settlement, excluding over-the-counter transactions, amounted to more than 65,495,000 yuan. In terms of settlement volume, aside from the 96 bonds, which had the most at approximately 9 million, the 22 Customs bonds surprisingly ranked second with over 7.1 million, and the Disarmament bonds also had 6.91 million. On the delivery side, aside from general arbitrageurs accounting for half, the majority was due to retail investors releasing bonds and being unable to recover them for delivery. On the receiving side, the majority was arbitrage by the financial sector, with the remainder being general giants, as they were easier to mortgage to banks.

Market Price History The lowest point was on October 17th, when salt tax was only 43.85 yuan, Disarmament bonds were 62.3 yuan, Finance Short-term bonds were 64.5 yuan, and Sixth-Year bonds were 59.5 yuan. At that time, the Italo-Ethiopian conflict, the potential involvement of Britain, the Japanese Dalian Conference, and the Shantou Japanese military incident all impacted market prices, leading to a crowded short position. However, starting that afternoon, the financial sector began to raise prices. At the time, there were rumors in the market that spot goods were extremely scarce. Upon investigation, it was found that the financial sector was still engaged in arbitrage and not actual receipt of goods. If this is true, future turbulent waves are yet to come. The rumors of currency reform, after a long period of circulation, suddenly materialized on November 4th. Neither the assassination of former President Wang, nor the Japanese naval incident on Searle Road, nor the recent North China Incident seemed to shake the confidence of the bulls. Market prices rose in a straight line, reaching new highs from November 21st to 24th. Salt tax reached 57.5 yuan, Disarmament bonds reached 85.5 yuan, Financial bonds reached 80.08 yuan, and Sixth-Year bonds reached 78.8 yuan, creating new highs unseen in recent years. Bullish investors advanced aggressively, extremely recklessly. Recently, Yin Rugeng's unusual actions have involved foreign affairs and are gradually expanding. The future turmoil is difficult to predict. The futures settlement and total transaction volume for November are listed below (unit: 100 yuan):

Grains High Prices Cause Buyers to Be Cautious Futures Flour and Wheat Remain Calm

The flour market showed a state of falling first and then stabilizing. At the initial opening, because the price of foreign wheat fluctuated by one jiao, market sentiment paid little attention. As the situation in North China entered a serious state, spot sales there seemed to have completely stopped. Although the inventory of factories was not abundant, because spot sales were quiet, each factory had a small amount of inventory. Therefore, market sentiment turned soft, and transactions also decreased. However, after the second round of trading, non-industry players came to absorb again, and near-term contracts recovered slightly, while far-term contracts recovered by about two fen. At the opening of the afternoon session, it was initially stable, but because rumors about the situation in North China became more prevalent, buyers became even more silent, and transactions were only around 200,000. Because the settlement for this month is approaching, the near-term is slightly more than two fen, and the far-term is slightly one fen. Looking at the subsequent situation, if spot sales are not smooth, the upward trend will be less than expected.
