Shen Bao Literary Weekly

Stone Carving

— Jiang Jing

I don’t know what kind of fate it is, but the children are enthusiastically carving stone seals.

Children have a very strong interest in new things. This interest is further heightened when they live a group life. If it is something they can't get, they will definitely find a way to get it. If it is something they can't do, they must try it. Even if you repeatedly warn them that it is a stupid or arrogant act.

Carving seals, when they can't even write characters properly, they naturally won't be able to do well. However, they insist on carving, and carve with great enthusiasm.

Ever since I wrote characters on a stone for one child, all the children who are carving seals know about it. They, who can't write characters, know that someone can write characters, and their joy is imaginable. So, sounds like "Teacher! Write for me" combined into a huge noise.

This trend was initially prevalent among older children. Because the difficulty of writing characters was removed, even younger children followed suit and started carving.

Writing characters is always my job. I seem to have become a responsive idol in a temple. As soon as class is over, they, regardless of whether you want to rest or not, rush to extend the stones (mostly unpolished stones) and shout eagerly, "Write for me! Teacher!" Some even don't have time to say the word "Teacher."

During the time from lunch to class, everyone is free. The children who want to write characters surround you in groups. The school originally has a disciplinary team to maintain order, but when they see them so crowded and shouting, they want to exercise their disciplinary authority. However, it is useless. The unanimous answer is almost entirely "I'm not asking you to write" and other similar words.

Once the characters are written, they run away one by one in a hurry, without stopping for a moment, pick up a knife and carve. Whether it is Chinese class or arithmetic class, this classroom or that classroom, there are always those children who are not afraid of the teacher's scolding, burying their heads in carving their seals.

They carved so frantically for three or four days, and I was surrounded by their frenzy for three or four days. In these few days, with the hands of one hundred and several dozen children, and five or six hundred stones (each person averaging at least four), sawing and grinding, the walls in the lane and the table tops in the classroom were covered with snow-white stone powder. — Until now, the ones in the classroom have long been wiped away, but the ones on the walls are still left as a memorial to their grand and enthusiastic activity.

Just when this activity was at its climax, the children's misfortune came! All their stones were confiscated by the teacher at each desk. It goes without saying that there were complaints everywhere. However, the teachers who confiscated also had their reasons: they soiled the walls and the table tops, which was unsightly; and what's more, they were carving even during class, which was a waste of their studies and could not be tolerated.

After this blow, the children were greatly disappointed. But still some children secretly come to ask me to write, and secretly carve.

Now, I myself no longer have this kind of crazy love for things, but I feel great joy for the children's activity this time. I keep thinking that if there are wise teachers who can grasp this precious interest of the children, take the opportunity to guide them, and make them abandon this carving of seals with a "private possession" nature, and turn to the carving of real things, it will definitely have good results. Perhaps among these children, one or two Rodin-like figures can be nurtured, which is not impossible. Even if not, even second-rate, or even worse, would be fine.

Every time I see the traces of stone powder on the wall, I always feel that my thoughts will definitely get true proof, and I am very disappointed!

Miscellaneous Notes on the Tokyo Film Industry

— Fang Xun

At the beginning of autumn, the real movie season has not yet begun, but the "Famous Films Week" held in a small cinema at that time fully aroused my desire to see it. However, firstly, because the doctor did not allow me to go to crowded places, and secondly, because the screening time conflicted with the hospital's schedule, but, during this week, I finally went twice without the doctor's knowledge. The rule of Japanese cinemas is to select two feature films for each screening, so what I saw were the German film "Dreaming Lips" (Der Traumende Mund) and the French film "Foreign Legion" (Le Grand Jen), which I probably will never have hope of seeing in China, and the American film "Cynan.a" directed by King Jidor and "Street Scenca." In "Dreaming Lips," what I wanted to see was just Elizabeth Bergner's acting skills. In "Foreign Legion," I wanted to see Jack Fede's direction. "Cynan.a" had been seen in the Lyceum in Shanghai, and seeing it again was just for Marion Irances's script, while "Street Scenca" was a film that I had missed in Shanghai due to circumstances and had been eagerly awaiting for two years without a re-release. Sure enough, this is a masterpiece unique to American films. After watching this film, I went back to find the script written by Emer Rriee. If I have the opportunity, I might want to translate this script and the film script. Among the so-called literary films I have seen, this film can be regarded as the most successful and unique. The "Famous Films Week" was held in a very small theater with only about four hundred seats. Of course, there were no air conditioning or ventilation facilities, and the seat prices were particularly fair, with each ticket costing two dimes and buying one getting one free, so the result was that it cost two jiao of Chinese money, a total of four excellent films to watch. Perhaps because it was a "Famous Film," the audience was all intellectuals, and most of them had an interest in film beyond that of a layman, so there was absolutely no talking during the screening, and some people even took notebooks to secretly record the scenes that they found interesting.

In terms of the system, Japanese cinemas are indeed very different from Chinese cinemas. In addition to the above-mentioned fact that each program screens two or even three feature films, most of them are continuous screening systems. As long as you are not afraid of a headache, you can sit inside for nine or ten hours with one ticket price. When they screen, except for the screenings at nine or ten in the morning on Sundays, most of them screen at noon every day and end at ten thirty in the afternoon. If you don't want to watch two films, then you can go after eight o'clock in the afternoon to buy a "discount" ticket, so when the gentlemen and ladies of Shanghai are having Dinner at Eight and leisurely going to the cinema at around 9:15, the ticket sellers and ushers in Tokyo cinemas have already patted the powder on their faces, changed their clothes, and gone to stroll on the Ginza streets with their matched friends. Thirdly, is the theater equipment. In terms of capacity, Tokyo has very large-scale places, such as the Japan Theater with 2,958 seats and the Hibiya Theater with 1,700 seats, etc., but their business slogan is only precise film selection and attentive service. Apart from these two, all unnecessary expenses are extremely frugal. Even the Japan Theater, which the Japanese boast as "the best in the Orient," has to let the Grand Theater and Cathay in Shanghai take a step in terms of splendor and fashion. Furthermore, the first-class "Imperial Theater" in Shinjuku is not even as good as the Lido and Guanglu, which screen second-run films in China. From these places, it can be seen that Chinese people, not to mention other things, are fully entitled to say that they have already stood at the very top of the world in terms of fashion and love of comfort.

With one or two exceptions, American films screened in Japan are usually more than half a year behind Shanghai. The reason for this may be for the purpose of making Japanese versions (that is, adding Japanese subtitles on the screen) — recently, they have gone a step further. In addition to making Japanese versions, they have also made "Japanese language versions," that is, removing the original sound and re-dubbing with Japanese narration. This time, P.C.L.'s trial product, Locke's Feet ficel, was a great success. Although there were many places that were "not synchronous," the cleverly translated dialogues fully compensated for these shortcomings. In the future, perhaps an era similar to the Japanese language will appear. — But there is one good thing about Japan, that is, you can see a wealth of European (excluding Soviet Russia) works. However, a few European and American films that were popular in Shanghai have suffered the misfortune of being banned in Japan, such as "The Private Life of Henry VIII," "Catherine the Great," "Madame Du Barry," etc. Even "The Merry Widow," which caused a sensation in Shanghai this time, suffered a cruel editing disaster. Why these films, which Shanghai people consider "nothing special," are banned, the reason can only be left to the intelligent readers to ponder for themselves.

To be honest, I don't have much expectation for Japanese films. The first film I saw after arriving in Tokyo, "Express Train," made me "unable to bear to finish watching" and I left halfway through. This is a extremely inferior work that is verbose, chaotic, and unable to even tell a story. The director, however, is Uehara Takehiko, who was already "quite famous" ten years ago! With decent equipment, even the most basic existing directors in China can make such a work. So I harbored some disrespectful feelings towards Japanese films. But a week ago, because the general newspapers excessively praised it, I finally went to the "Japan Theater" mentioned above to see a film called "Two Wives." As a work of art, this is by no means a praiseworthy work, but in terms of technology and acting skills alone, this can indeed be said to be a very decent sound film that has reached world standards. The original work is by the popular writer Nakano Minoru, the director is Naruse Mikio, and the actors are the famous actors of the former Tsukiji Little Theater, Maruyama Sadao, Hanabusa Yae, and P.C.L.'s new junior Chiba Tokuko. (The names of Maruyama and Hanabusa reminded me of the pleasant Tokyo days. His outstanding performance as Lopakhin in Chekhov's famous play "The Cherry Orchard" in Sakae-za is still clearly remembered!) The content of the story is about a man who marries a female singer and has a daughter. Because of incompatibility, he separates from his wife, and later marries a woman from a geisha background in the northern country and has children. At the beginning of the film, the daughter born to the first wife has reached the age of engagement. In order to ask her father to come forward to handle the marriage, she volunteers to go to Shinshu to find her father. In her expectation, she thought that her father and his second wife must be living a life of pleasure, but when she arrived there, the facts were completely contrary to her expectations. Her stepmother is a very "virtuous" woman who not only loves her husband, but also secretly sends money to the first wife in Tokyo every month without her husband's knowledge. She feels that she should not take her father away from this kind family, so after her father handles her marriage in Tokyo, she does not retain him on behalf of her mother and lets her father return. Judging from the story, the author's worldview is still hovering in the late Meiji and early Taisho eras. Today, it can be said that it has a hint of commonality with the Women's Association's advocacy of "wise wife and good mother" promoted by the military. Here, the director only uses the perspective of the daughter of the first wife (who should be a modern woman in appearance) to observe the relationship between men and women in the Meiji era without any opinion. He not only does not add any criticism or explanation, but even greatly admires the wise wife and good mother and gives it full praise. This is why this film can only make people happy but cannot make people feel deeply. However, in terms of acting skills, direction, and especially the use of radio, we must not underestimate its success. I don't understand, why, with such material and human environments, are they not producing some higher-level works?

In addition to P.C.L., Shochiku, Nikkatsu, and Shinko all have domestically produced aftersound machines, but in essence, except for P.C.L.'s machine, which is slightly better than the celebrity's machine, Nikkatsu's is similar to China's Sanyou type and even Zhonghua Tong type, and the emerging Oriental Sy-stem is only at the level of a Chinese self-made radio a year ago.

For the film "Two Wives," I waited in the drizzle for almost half an hour. Since the beginning of autumn, it is said that this "Japan Theater" has encountered "business as terrible as murder." Most Japanese cinemas sell tickets without restrictions, so when passing through Yurakucho, you often see the struggle of "seats are full, only three seats are available," but the people buying tickets are still meandering like a long snake. Also seeing a glimpse of the magic of this script.

The "Poetry Revolution" in the Late Qing Dynasty

— Chen Zizhan

In the late Qing Dynasty, there was a so-called "Poetry Revolution" in literature, which was corresponding to the so-called "Reform Movement" in politics. In other words, there was a reform movement in politics before there was a reform movement in literature. In fact, the poetry revolution at that time was only a reform, not a revolution. Moreover, the political reform failed, and the literary reform also failed.

This is a long story, so I can only say it briefly.

The reformists in literature were also the reformists in politics, such as Tan Sitong, Xia Zengyou, Liang Qichao, and Huang Zunxian. Of course, Kang Youwei also belonged to this faction, but he initially only paid attention to politics. It was only after the political failure that he paid attention to writing poetry. Moreover, he was more mature and steady. No matter how new he was in poetry, there were limits after all.

Tan Sitong can be regarded as the first vanguard general of the reformists. He did not lose the stubbornness of the Hunan people. He failed in politics and refused to escape. This is the rebellious spirit of a revolutionary and the martyrdom spirit of a religious person. It is a pity that he was killed. His so-called "new learning" poetry, like his new political ideals, did not fulfill his original aspirations.

Xia Zengyou had not yet run onto the political stage. Fortunately, he did not die with Tan Sitong, but unfortunately, he never dared to come forward again in the literary reform movement. Of course, his new learning poetry, only "snatching new terms" and "new contract words, endlessly at the tip of the pen," even his companions like Liang Qichao said "impossible to understand," which shows that it was conceivable that he would never get through it if he continued. Liang Qichao said that "at that time in the motherland, there was not a single book on philosophy, politics, and law to read. Two or three of us claimed to be the first to get the atmosphere, but the level of our thinking was like this." This is indeed an honest statement. Their reform movement, whether political or literary, ended in failure. Although it is said that it was due to the objective environment that did not allow it, and the subjective strength was not enough, it cannot be said that this was not a major reason.

Although the political reform of 1898 failed, because of the invasion of the Eight-Nation Alliance in 1900, the autocratic Qing government thought of holding a few "new policies" again. In short, after three very painful experiences in 1894, 1898, and 1900, a little new dawn seemed to be revealed in politics again. At the same time, in literature, no, in poetry, being able to slightly reflect the politics and society of this painful era, and being able to be representative of the poetry of this era, we have to promote Huang Zunxian's Renjinglu Poetry Draft for a little achievement in the so-called "poetry revolution".

After Huang Zunxian failed in politics, he closed his doors to read and write poetry. He was considered a new figure who slightly understood the international situation at that time. He had been a diplomat for many years, and he had been to Japan, India, Nanyang, the United States, and other places. He was one of the most knowledgeable and learned among the reformers. Since he was not successful in politics, he put all his energy into poetry. Therefore, his achievements in poetry were greater than anyone else at the same time. Liang Qichao said that "among modern poets who can melt new ideals into old styles, Huang Gongdu is the most worthy." This is correct. Strictly speaking, he is still only a reformist in the poetry world, not a revolutionary. Because he is still circling in the old style. However, his poetry materials are slightly richer than those of the ancients. He not only occasionally adopts dialects and proverbs, but he can also "write down whatever objects, uncharted realms, and experiences of the ear and eye the ancients did not have." It is a pity that his hearing and sight are limited, and what he writes is not much. As for what he said: "I write what I say, the ancient halls can restrain. Even if it is colloquial, I will register it on silk. People five thousand years later will be surprised to see it as ancient and colorful." He himself did not truly practice this proposition of his. His Nine Mountain Songs, although imitating the tunes of folk songs, are only occasional attempts. Later, Mr. Hu Shi's vernacular poems in his Collection of Experiments can be said to be the implementation of Huang Zunxian's proposition of "I write what I say." If we want to regard Huang Zunxian as a pioneer of the "poetry revolution," he really has the spirit and courage of a pioneer. Kang Youwei's theory of poetry is that "new worlds and bizarre realms are born, and new sounds are created by searching Europe and Asia." In fact, his poetry is only in the old style, not a new sound. It is not considered that he has grasped this bizarre new world, and it is in vain to have traveled around the world. As for what he said, "the artistic conception is almost without Li Du, and where do I put Yuan and Ming in my eyes," it may be true that he did not learn the poems of the Yuan and Ming people. He could not learn from Li Du, even though he had read Du Ji. Some people put him on a par with Huang Zunxian because he had been the leader of the political reformists.

In those days, Huang Zunxian's "new poetry style" was famous, and Liang Qichao's "new prose style" was even more famous. Mr. Liang was famous all over the world, but he had no reputation as a poet. He did not like to write poetry, but he liked to talk about poetry. In his poems, he advocated patriotism, martial arts, reform, self-reliance, civil rights, and equality, which was generally similar to Huang Zunxian and other new school poets. He did not express complaints or groans in his poems, but loved to say exaggerated personal words and actively enterprising words, which was different from any other poet at the same time. He said, "If I don't write poetry today, then that's it. If I write poetry, I must be the Columbus and Magellan of the poetry world before it is possible. It is like the land of Europe has been prosperous, and new lands must be sought in America and along the Pacific coast. If you want to be the Columbus and Magellan of the poetry world, you must have three strengths: First, you must have a new artistic conception; second, you must have new words and sentences; and you must also enter it in the style of the ancients, and then it will become poetry." This is what he said when he was traveling in Honolulu in 1898. It has been nearly forty years, and today it seems to be a shallow and ordinary remark, but at that time, it had a different meaning. He knew that he had to "try his best to import the spirit and thoughts of Europe to provide the poetry materials for the future." He knew that "if China does not have a poetry revolution, then the fate of poetry will be exhausted." He knew that "the opportunity for revolution is gradually ripening." In the literary revolution, he cannot be regarded as the first prophet. It is a pity that he almost put all his energy on political commentary. Although he created a "new prose style," he did not create a new poetry style. If he had been willing to write more poetry, with his talent and unrestrained writing, and established a little momentum for the so-called poetry revolution since Tan Sitong and Xia Zengyou, it would have been greater than what Huang Zunxian had established, I think it is possible.

In all fairness, this "Poetry Revolution" cannot but be said to have failed. However, in this experience of failure, we were given several very valuable lessons. First, they originally wanted to "melt new ideals into old styles." In other words, they wanted to put new content into old forms. As a result, we know that if the form does not change, some new content cannot be put in. To express the new phenomena and new ideas of this great era, it is necessary to create a new form, even though the old poetry style still has its uses in certain situations. Second, they are still officials and intellectuals. Their "Poetry Revolution" was to promote the "reform" of the monarchical politics, and to shout for their own class; it was not to serve the public, and their poems had nothing to do with the public. Of course, the public at that time, the more aware public, would not support their movement either. What's more, the awakening of the public still relies on poetry and other literary departments, and even the entire cultural education, to jointly fulfill the responsibility of arousing it! Third, they wanted to adopt dialects and proverbs close to the public to write poetry, and although they did not practice it, this theory is correct.

As for the opinions and works of this group of poets, there are citations and introductions in my books: "Changes in Modern Chinese Literature" and "A History of Chinese Literature in the Last Thirty Years." I will not repeat them here.

There are also those who stood on the opposite side of this new school of poets and can be regarded as pure old school poets, such as the retro school Wang Lanyun. He said that his poems were just "a hodgepodge of imitations," which is correct. He said, "Everything is new in the last fifty years, and the lines will surely be startling." But he did not write any startling poems that could be praised for contemporary new things. There was also the so-called "Tongguang Style" of Shen Zengzhi, Chen Sanli, etc. Originally, some poets during the Tongzhi and Guangxu years promoted the study of Song poetry, and the poetry of the Huangshangu and Wangjinggong schools, which became a trend for a time. Some people called it the "Song Poetry Movement." This movement was a step backward, while the poetry revolution movement was progressive. Those who went backward had to imitate a certain generation, a certain school, or a certain person in ancient times when writing poetry; those who were more progressive wanted to adopt the spirit and thoughts of modern Europeans as poetry materials and did not hesitate to start their own schools. Those who went backward had to fill in difficult words and create awkward sentences when writing poetry; those who were more progressive wanted to use dialects and proverbs, and wanted to use new terms and new sentences when writing poetry. There were also the talented people Fan Fanshan and Yi Shifu. Their poems were greedy for quantity and competed for skill, showing off their romanticism. They liked to stack rhymes a lot, liked to make clever antithetical couplets, liked to praise actors, and liked to play with women. They lived a decadent life of enjoyment, and poetry was a record of this life. Among the old school poets, they were the most depraved. In short, after these many old school poets' spiritual works, all the disadvantages of old style poetry were exposed. It seems that the poetry revolution movement was able to survive thanks to their help. Therefore, Huang Zunxian became the only great poet in the late Qing Dynasty.

A Short Account of Climbing the Mountain at Dusk

— Shen Shengshi

The golden light of the setting sun splashed the mountain slopes red.

All three of us loved climbing mountains at dusk.

The mountain slope was quietly devoid of tourists. Among the massive rocks, the three of us seemed like three small crawling insects. The magnificence of the mountain highlighted the insignificance of life.

Huge rocks, like gigantic monsters, squatted on the mountainside, their faces covered in mossy patches. As we climbed, our feet slipped, refusing to be controlled, so we clung tightly to clumps of weeds, carefully ascending.

Halfway up, I embraced a massive boulder, foolishly searching for traces of history from thousands of years past. However, the stone face bore only rough marks, a weathered and ancient countenance.

We climbed together to a large grotto, where we sat down to rest. Above us was the vast sky. Looking into the distance, the twilight, like a thin mist, descended from all sides, descending, descending. A purplish-dark cloud lingered over the smoky trees, gradually blending together. A vast expanse of city streets and villages also sank into the hazy obscurity.

After the setting sun had completely faded, the mountain wind brought a chilling coolness.

Looking up at the high peaks, huge rocks piled upon rocks, crowded together, the mountain color turned purplish-dark, and the mountain wind brought a chilling, gloomy air.

Dusk enveloped the mountain, and an atmosphere of coldness pressed in on us.

In the foolish silence of the three of us, I searched for the stars leaking out from the edge of the sky. One, two, sparsely.

Let's climb down before it gets completely dark.

The mountain night is filled with dark and cold thoughts. A sense of coldness touches the heart.

A friend said:

The mountain at night is not suitable for an ordinary person to stay. In the faint moonlight, graceful immortals from myths come out for a night stroll, floating ethereally. Groups of three or two celestial children sing on the mountainside. This scene is truly an ideal beauty.

Clinging to tree trunks and exposed roots, we climbed down. The sky was already dark, and the small protruding stones on the mountain path under our feet were not clearly visible. A moment of carelessness could cause a stumble. Everyone called out, feeling for the path we had come up. Unnoticed, huge rocks squatted like giant demons, blocking our way.

When we reached the foot of the mountain, sweat had soaked everyone's foreheads, and the soles of our feet were burning.

Looking back at the mountain peak, a crescent moon slowly ascended from the deep blue horizon.

Brothers Who Didn’t Turn in Their Uniforms

Life

— Mo Fu

Life is a rubber bladder. If you don't have some backbone, it will shrink and constrict you tightly, to an unimaginably small extent. At the same time, it can be stretched to infinite proportions, even if it is empty inside, leaving most people unable to grasp the boundaries and unable to guess what treasures it contains.

One gloomy, cold morning, I was still lying in bed, haphazardly thinking about things that I myself wasn't entirely clear about. A long-lost acquaintance suddenly arrived, just as he had when he left this place, without leaving a trace.

"Ah!" he exclaimed in surprise, as if he had seen something frightening. "I thought you had already left here. I was just coming to see if I could find you..."

He didn't allow me to reply, repeating several times, "How did you manage to stay here?..."

"How did I manage? ... Twenty-four hours a day."

Beyond that, I couldn't say anything more specific or detailed.

His question prompted me to think about the question—how did I manage to stay here? I certainly hadn't realized it. I had neither the skills nor the opportunity to produce anything, and moreover—here I want to quote a line from the Greek poet Marcus Argentarius: "...A person who has nothing has no friends!" In this situation, I never expected to stay so long. Looking back, it's simply a chaotic dream. When I was hungry, I found a way to get credit at a restaurant; when the landlord demanded rent, I tried my best to stall; and I even managed to coax kerosene from the bridge watchman; and I tricked (perhaps this word is the most appropriate, but he trusted me a lot) coal briquettes from the Yi Xishan Red Coal Factory; and somewhere, even though it was to be expected, I unexpectedly received some extra money. And so, all year round... wow, it's a miracle!

"What are your plans for the future?"

"What can I do? ... I take it one day at a time."

After a brief account of our separation, he left in a hurry. The warmth he brought was taken away with him. My small room remained cold.

Standing there blankly, observing the things around me, I smiled—I felt like I really smiled.

"Anyway, I will continue to live, I must continue to live, I have the right to live, ... until the end of my life."

An Ode to Shenzhen

— Li Sanlang

Winding around the nine-bend bridge;

There is a dog racing track there,

There is a gambling den,

All day, all night,

Seductive songs are swirling.

Red neon lights,

Dazzling brilliance;

Also, women's breasts,

Hazy night,

Can't see the lonely stars in the sky,

Can't see the misery of the people in the semi-colony.

This is just a scene of intense frenzy.

Shenzhen! is a paradise for pleasure-seekers,

Is a vast and fertile square.

The oppressors' flags are fluttering,

On the tracks of the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway.

But, it's no use going in without money,

It only welcomes—

High-class Chinese, compradors,

A soulless crowd.

Using our homeland,

Using our labor,

Developing it day by day,

Hong Kong, Kowloon, Shenzhen,

Look! Whose paradise of pleasure is that?

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

"Aspiring to Save the Country"

— Li Min

Yin Rugeng, the administrative inspector of the Luan-Yu district in Hebei Province, betrayed the country, declared independence, established the so-called Jidong Anti-Communist Committee, appointed himself as the chairman, and severed ties with the country. The national government has now ordered a campaign to suppress him. However, according to a report in the newspaper the other day, Yin Rugeng even told reporters that this move was "aimed at saving the country." This is truly "the greatest absurdity under heaven." If this can be called aspiring to save the country, then what is the difference between betraying the country and saving it? With this kind of interpretation of saving the country, we really feel at a loss as to where to begin saving the country.

A traitor does not necessarily claim to be a traitor. He can use all kinds of means to betray the country, but he will never openly say that he is betraying the country. He will surely use some nice-sounding terms or pretexts to cover up his treacherous behavior, and may even say that he is saving the country. This is a common practice throughout history, both in China and abroad. Zheng Xiaoxu was truly acting as someone else's slave, but he would never admit that he was acting as a slave. Perhaps he would say that he was being "loyal to the former dynasty" and wanted to "rescue the people from fire and water." Would a thief admit to being a thief? No matter how shameful and despicable his actual actions may be, he can always say something beautiful. Yin Rugeng is just one of these people. Moreover, compared to other great traitors (such as Zheng Xiaoxu), he is truly insignificant!

However, will the shamelessness and baseness of these people, because of their skillful cover-ups, mean that their true nature will never be discovered by us? No, that's not the case. It depends on whether the actual actions of these people match their words. Yin Rugeng sings loudly about "aspiring to save the country," but the things he is doing are clearly betraying the country. Who can be deceived by this? Saving the country requires facts! No matter how you try to cover up treacherous actions, people can still see them very clearly. Who would believe that Yin Rugeng is truly "aspiring to save the country"? People's eyes are sharp!

There are many people like Yin Rugeng active before our eyes. Unfortunately, the national government's decree of suppression only applies to Yin Rugeng alone. I can't help but feel wronged for Yin Rugeng!

Arranging a Marriage (Continued)

— Shen Qianli

(III)

"Haha, mother and daughter are different after all. You have private things to say, so you run outside to talk!"

"What are you doing here, Yun'er?" Her face was as tight as a drum.

"Runweng! You're going to scare her! You can't do that!" He laughed dryly.

"No, I'm not joking with her," he said seriously, his face expressionless, like a father scolding his son. "I'll be honest with you. If you want to marry me, just give up on that poor kid. Don't associate with him anymore. Otherwise, your mother still owes me two hundred yuan. I can marry a woman anywhere I go..."

"Alright, Runweng! Don't scare her. How could such a beautiful girl like her be hooking up with those poor kids? Sigh! I still thought you were a terrestrial immortal. You're worrying too much for an immortal..." The speaker's small eyes glanced sideways at the gentleman's face, and seeing that he was unmoved by her words, she stopped speaking.

"This is your mother here. Marrying you wouldn't mean you'd suffer any grievances," he said, taking a sip of hot tea, followed by a "hiss." The smell of tobacco made Yunying, who was standing not far from him, consciously take a step back. He didn't seem to notice and continued seriously, "At first, I told your mother that if you agreed to marry me, I wouldn't ask her to repay the two hundred yuan. I'd also give her an additional hundred yuan as a bride price. From then on, we'd be relatives. If she has nothing to do, she can help me a little and have a free meal at my house. Don't you think this idea suits your wishes?" A hint of a smile flashed across his face, but he immediately suppressed it when Yunying looked up.

"Runweng! You're really an old hand at romance, thinking of everything in such excruciating detail! We're truly ashamed of ourselves! Haha..."

"Everything that Master Run does is right. It's just that I was born with a hard life, and I only raised such a daughter." Tears welled up in her eyes, secretly flowing.

"You only have this one daughter. No one is going to eat her, what are you crying about?" Her words cut off her lament like a knife. "It's not that I'm afraid people will eat her. If she follows Master Run, would anyone dare to touch a hair on her head? I'm just saying that she's seventeen years old this year and has never left my side for a moment. She doesn't understand anything and I'm afraid she won't be able to serve Master Run in the future and will make you angry!" Her vocal cords seemed to have snapped, and she couldn't help but sob.

"Mom, you promised him, what are you still crying about? I'll just have to accept my fate!" She glared at the gentleman, her expression as hard as iron.

At this moment, he jumped out of bed involuntarily, grabbed her arm, and brought his withered face close to hers. His bones seemed to have softened halfway as he bent over and hugged her tightly. "Good girl, how did your mother give you such a sharp tongue? All the anger in my belly was driven away by your few words. Come here, don't upset me anymore. Come, give me a kiss, give me a kiss..."

"No, no, this won't do. What will it look like?" She curled up her head and face like a hedgehog, holding her hands tightly.

"Alright, Master Run! If you push her too hard, she'll get angry!" A tear fell in the middle of her words. "Haha... a daughter is still a daughter, a son-in-law should be different..." Another burst of laughter. (End)

(Yesterday, due to space constraints, it was not possible to publish it. I would like to apologize to the author and readers.)

Snow

— Luo Zhihua

Last winter, I lived in a small town. It was surrounded by severe cold all day long. In the morning, when I opened the window and looked out, a vast white expanse of snow unfolded. Facing this frank snowfield, my melancholy heart immediately put on a layer of cheerful tune.

A friend and I lived on the third floor of a house. This house was a relative's villa, outside the town. He moved here in the summer, and in the winter he still lived in his town residence. I came down from the university and couldn't find a job. My relative meant for me to stay here and have fun. Anyway, the family hadn't gone bankrupt at that time. I lived with this friend: he returned from Beijing to this small town, and was also very lonely. Being together might be better—each doing his own thing, and when there was nothing to do, we'd play together.

But we really didn't have anything to do, we spent about half our time this way.

One morning, I was preparing to write a letter to my older brother in Shanghai when he came in. He was wearing an apricot-yellow morning gown and sat on the sofa. He didn't like to talk, even though we were together. There wasn't much conversation. For example, he read the newspaper all day, but I didn't. To be honest, I didn't have the courage to read the newspaper. Every day, even in this small town, robberies occurred frequently. The news would make you sick, so why look at it? But he had to read the newspaper.

"Fourteen people were executed yesterday! All of them were young—only one was an old man in his fifties!"

His face was very calm, like a cup of still white water. He seemed to be trying to stir my heart, but in reality, I hated listening to it. Moreover, this kind of cliché news had lost its stimulating effect. On my dull eardrums, he would no longer be moved by it. I looked at his face, nodded my head, and pushed one of the two cups of milk that his nanny had prepared for him.

"It's going to get cold soon—drink it and go out for a run. The snow scene is very beautiful today!"

Maybe he could tell that I didn't like hearing these things, because he didn't continue speaking. I told him that in this era, we were just supporting actors, not important at all. Let the world change as it may. No matter what kind of world it becomes, we useless people will still be useless. Moreover, a person like him, who lacks courage, shouldn't worry. I understood this world very well. I had read about it in my university courses. But, I was still playing the role of a supporting character. I didn't want to be a protagonist and take on the task of changing this era. He listened to my words, was spoken to by me, and drank the milk. He said to me:

"There's another piece of news that's a bit related to you!

"Another piece of news related to me? Let's go!"

I said to him nonchalantly. So, we listened to the sound of silence in the snow, and looked back. A long trail of footprints was hidden in the white. Facing the shining snow, looking at the distant trees and the sea-blue sky, I sang a poem by Shelley, and he sang Heine's "Struggle Song," his voice high and excited, which surprised me, given his usually quiet throat.

Climbing mountains in the snow is the most interesting thing. It's like a person searching for his own path in a pool of blood. We climbed mountains, climbed trees, and a whole morning passed. Our bodies were hot, full of heat.

On the way back, I went to another friend's house, and he went back by himself.

When I returned home, it was already dusk. The distant mountain shadows were faintly visible in the white.

The nanny gave me a letter:

"Old Zhang: I'm leaving. You said I didn't have courage, I'll try to have it. Maybe I will.

Here's a piece of news about you. I hope you'll read it?

See you later. I wish you good fortune. Jin."

"When did she give it to you?"

"This afternoon."

I sat on the sofa and read the newspaper article. It said that the bank in Shanghai where my older brother worked had gone bankrupt. There was also another article saying that things were very tight everywhere these days: the end of the year was approaching, bankruptcies, executions, were happening everywhere.

Did he leave because of this? Yes, he left because of this. The next day, I received a telegram from my older brother saying that he was preparing to return to this small town immediately to take refuge. However, the next day's newspaper said that he had been detained.

So, I left that place and came here. Living here, without milk, without a nanny, I am "living."

Page 16

Morning

— Bin

My wife took the shopping basket to the kitchen, leaving the child in the room. Recently, I lost my job and have been idle at home, so I moved out an old bookshelf. It's full of books that I like, but since I bought them, I've never had time to flip through more than a few pages. Now that I'm stuck at home all day, I want to dig up some new knowledge from them as a spiritual compensation after losing my job. But in the morning, my wife came back from shopping for groceries and went to the kitchen to cook. The child was shut up in this small bedroom, making trouble everywhere. Either he broke something, or he fell and cried loudly. There wasn't a minute of quiet to let me flip through a few pages of a book. Because of this, I bought a pile of cheap toys for him to play with on his own. For the past few days, thanks to these new things, the child has been quietly playing with the toys in a corner without making a sound. But these few cheap toys, after three or five days, have become a pile of unsightly garbage, and the child has returned to his normal state. Today, he was making noise again, and I gave him a beating, but my wife heard the crying and ran upstairs to nag. She said angrily that I was useless, that a man couldn't earn money and instead stayed at home all day beating the child. Later, she even said that marrying me was her bad luck. In a fit of anger, she picked up the child and went downstairs.

After losing my job, relatives and friends also lost that kind of mutually supportive relationship between human beings. Staying at home is naturally not what I want, but I can no longer afford to visit relatives and friends. As soon as they see your face, it's as if your expression tells them that you're there to borrow money. Before you can even open your mouth, you can hear a string of complaints about the bad economy and how hard it is to do business, their faces drawn tight, as if a disaster is about to befall them, making you feel like you're sitting on pins and needles, too embarrassed to freeload a meal. I understand this art of living. Poverty is still my own. Reading a book is better than chatting at a friend's house anyway, but women have their own incomprehensible logic. This is my first new discovery.

But the fact is that in this society where economic relations maintain order, a husband has an obligation to support his wife. Staying at home reading broken books after losing my job makes me seem out of touch. So, I put on my felt hat and went out onto the street.

It's already winter, and the plane trees along the road are all bald. The sun shines on my thin cotton robe, and I feel a kind of warm comfort. After wandering past a few streets, I thought about a place where I could sit for a while, a place that wouldn't see me as a tactless debt collector. My mind flipped through a record book, going through all the relatives and friends I knew, one by one. But when their ugly faces appeared before me, I generously discarded them one by one. Finally, inspired by a school, I went straight to the house of a former professor.

At school, the professor was very fond of me. He often liked me to go to his house to chat. The professor's wife knew that I was her husband's prized student and was especially warm and welcoming. Even when the professor wasn't home, she would keep me for dinner and chat. I rang the doorbell of that small Western-style house, almost as if I had discovered a treasure. The professor himself came to open the door. When he saw me, he pushed up his rimless glasses and hugged me into the house like a child, while shouting his wife's name loudly. The professor was really very happy. He said that he missed our classmates very much. He said that between teachers and students at school, they still had to maintain a layer of dignity, but after graduation, they should visit each other often like family. He said many things in one breath, things that I hadn't heard from anyone in the past few months. When the professor's wife stepped into the parlor, he began to ask about my recent situation. My answer stunned him. He subconsciously pushed up his glasses again and said, "The dead end of the intellectual class, the dead end of the intellectual class! I haven't seen a single one of my students achieve the kind of position in society that I hoped for. No wonder the number of students in schools decreases every year. Universal education is really easier said than done!" The professor paced the parlor with emotion.

The professor's wife told me that the number of students was decreasing every year, and the school's funds were insufficient to cover expenses. They were already three months behind on salary! I looked at the professor's face, that long face. I thought I should leave. I don't need complaints and sympathy. This society, or rather this world, no longer has a place where I can sit for a while.

When I returned home, the child climbed onto the table and grabbed the food with his fingers. The sun was already high overhead. The morning had passed. What about the afternoon? Still that endless series of days following behind you?

Ballads

The Three Smiles of Xia Hesheng

Dunben (800) 7 PM to 8 PM

Opening: "Bao Yu Cries for Qing Wen"

The best of the maids in Grand View Garden. Jade shattered, fragrance vanished, buried underground. The sentimental young master howls and weeps. His heart full of melancholy, all thoughts turned to ash. Ignorant little maids speak rashly, saying, she, played in the mortal realm for only twenty-eight years. A jade maiden descended from the ninth heaven. Crying for you, serene, dignified, virtuous, and prudent. Fit to scold, fit to smile, you pleased my heart. Crying for you, with unparalleled intelligence and ingenious mind. With penetrating and sharp understanding, you were truly talented. Crying for you, with a straightforward and upright heart like a man, innocent and genuine, like a child. Qing Wen, which of the four beauties can compare to you? Among women, past and present, you can be called the best. We relied on each other, morning and night, for only a few years. How did I accumulate such ill fortune to have a fairy accompany my impure jade? Qing Wen, sometimes I recited books on freezing winter days. Only you, kept me company all night, unafraid of the cold. Qing Wen, sewing a fur coat while ill, your care was so profound. Each thread was made with painstaking effort. Qing Wen, the Wang family hag truly deserves to die. Spreading rumors and daring to slander. Qing Wen, madam listened to malicious gossip. Forced you to return, like boiling cranes and burning zithers. I stood by, silently, it shouldn't have been. It's like, forcing Yang Guifei to death at Mawei. Qing Wen, your pleas were ineffective, you left in sorrow. Saying how, a beautiful face is a cause of misfortune. Qing Wen, your wronged soul returned to the immortal ranks. Still doing, the happy flower goddess, returning to the uncarved jade. Qing Wen, the garden is desolate, no one notices. Only I, the master of Yi Hong Courtyard, alone know sorrow. After weeping, I burn paper money. The ghostly wind is bleak, the night is growing late. My hair stands on end, I quietly return.

Pan Yousheng stops Chen Jiazhen's business and wants to tell Yuan Meiyun, and he said it when inviting her to be the bridesmaid, how wonderful. I wonder what Yuan Meiyun felt in her heart, and I wonder if Yuan Meiyun had anything else to say at the time?

"Boatwoman" Premieres Today

Free Songsheets and Scales

Directed by Shen Xiling, starring Gao Zhanfei, Xu Lai, and Sun Min, the all-dialogue and singing sound film "Boatwoman," recently produced by the Mingxing Film Company, is scheduled to premiere today at the Jincheng Theater on Beijing Road. In order to enhance the audience's interest and increase their knowledge of film, a copy has been reprinted, and 10,000 pieces of scales have been cut from this copy, along with a finely printed songbook (containing "West Lake Spring Dawn," "Boat Song," and "Goddess Song"), which will be given to the audience with the Jincheng Theater tickets. The company will first pre-select 50 feet and keep them safe. After the event, the scale with the selected portion will be revealed. If any audience member receives a scale identical to the selected one, they will receive a photograph of the protagonist of "Boatwoman" (as specified by the audience member). However, the interest can be greatly increased by comparing the scale with the action on the screen. However, due to restrictions, the photographs will be given out until they are gone. Therefore, those who wish to obtain the scales and the photograph of the protagonist of "Boatwoman" are requested to be quick to arrive first so as not to regret being too late. The songbook is not limited. It is also rumored that "Boatwoman" will have a public screening at the Jincheng Theater at 10 AM this morning, and invitations have been sent to people from all walks of life to attend.

Mingxing's New Film "Boatwoman"

— Directed by Shen Xiling, starring Gao Zhanfei, Xu Lai, and Sun Min

New Film Introductions

East Wind and Begonia

Chinese and foreign movie fans consider Joan Crawford to be the standard modern daughter. She recently married Franchot Tone. The story of their love has long been a world-famous tale, and Joan boldly displays a new posture in her latest masterpiece, "East Wind and Begonia," especially opening up a new path for the study of "kisses." The supporting male lead is the Scottish tough guy Brian Aherne, and the humorous master of "The Gay Divorcee," Frank Morgan, also participates. The film is produced by MGM and is now showing in Nanjing.

The Dark Angel

Guy Bolton's world-famous play "The Dark Angel" has now been produced by United Artists and translated as "Tears on the Land of Longing." It is a collaboration between Frederic March, the cinematic genius of literary works such as "Resurrection" and "Les Misérables," British standard beauty Merle Oberon, and Herbert Marshall, who recently co-starred with Garbo. The poignant and glamorous nature of the play is no less than that of China's Dream of the Red Chamber and Romance of the West Chamber, so European and American men and women often regard it as a sacred book for discussing love. Therefore, it goes without saying that its screen performance can resonate with the hearts of lovers around the world. The director of the film is Sidney Franklin, the director of massive productions such as "The Good Earth" and "Smilin' Through."

Rendesvouz

Since the First World War, international espionage and counter-espionage in Washington when the United States entered the war were extremely active. The book "Black Chamber" provides a comprehensive overview of this situation. The book was originally a secret treasure translated worldwide. MGM selected the most exciting parts of the book, including the secret assembly of the Allied naval and land forces, and the German adoption of submarine policies using espionage to steal American radio telegrams to carry out threats of surprise attacks, and filmed them into a film called "Rendesvouz," now translated as "Washington's Big Secret." Starring William Powell, it is truly a rare and great military espionage film.

In addition, Weissmuller of "Tarzan the Ape Man" will again co-star with Maureen O'Sullivan in a "Tarzan" film originally titled "The Tarzan Escapes," which is more magnificent and exciting than "Tarzan and His Mate." Movie fans at sea, wait and see. (According to the "Tarzan" series of films, there is now a new film starring world sports champion Herman Brix, called "New Adventures of Tarzan," which is well worth seeing and will be shown at the Grand Shanghai.)
